DTS, INC.
5220 Las Virgenes Road

Calabasas, California 91302
(818) 436-1000

Dear Stockholder:

We cordially invite you to attend a special meeting of stockholders of DTS, Inc. (“we,” “us,” “our” or “DTS”) to be held at the
Westlake Village Inn, 31943 Agoura Road, Westlake Village, California 91361, at 8:00 a.m., local time, on December 1, 2016 (the
“special meeting”). Holders of record of DTS’s common stock, par value $0.0001 per share, at the close of business on October 20,
2016 (the “record date”) will be entitled to vote at, or any adjournment or postponement of, the special meeting.

At the special meeting, we will ask you to vote on a proposal (the “merger proposal”) to adopt the Agreement and Plan of Merger
(the “merger agreement”), dated as of September 19, 2016, among Tessera Technologies, Inc., a Delaware corporation (“Tessera”),
DTS, Tempe Holdco Corporation, a Delaware corporation and wholly owned subsidiary of Tessera (“Holdco”), Tempe Merger Sub
Corporation, a Delaware corporation and wholly owned subsidiary of Holdco (“Parent Merger Sub”) and Arizona Merger Sub
Corporation, a Delaware corporation and wholly owned subsidiary of Holdco (“Company Merger Sub,” and together with Parent
Merger Sub, the “Merger Subs”). Under the merger agreement, and subject to its terms and conditions, Company Merger Sub will
merge with and into DTS (the “DTS merger”), with DTS as the surviving corporation.

At the effective time of the DTS merger, you will be entitled to receive $42.50 in cash, without interest and less any required tax
withholdings, for each share of DTS common stock that you own, and, thereafter, you will have no ownership interest in the continuing
business of DTS, Tessera or Holdco. Completion of the DTS merger requires, among other things, the adoption of the merger
agreement by the affirmative vote of the holders of a majority of the outstanding shares of our common stock as of the record date.

DTS’s board of directors reviewed and considered the terms and conditions of the DTS merger and unanimously determined that
the DTS merger is fair to, advisable and in the best interests of DTS and its stockholders, unanimously approved the merger agreement
and the other transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, including the DTS merger, and resolved to submit and recommend
the adoption of the merger agreement and the approval of the transactions contemplated thereby, including the DTS merger, to DTS’s
stockholders. DTS’s board of directors made its determination after considering a number of factors more fully described in the
accompanying proxy statement. DTS’s board of directors unanimously recommends that you vote “FOR” the merger proposal.

We are also asking you to vote on (i) a proposal to approve, on a non-binding, advisory basis, merger-related compensation for
DTS’s named executive officers (the “merger-related compensation proposal”) and (ii) a proposal to adjourn the special meeting, if
necessary or appropriate, to solicit additional proxies if there are not sufficient votes at the time of the special meeting to approve the
merger proposal (the “adjournment proposal”). DTS’s board of directors unanimously recommends that you vote “FOR” each of
these proposals.

We will transact no other business at the special meeting, except such business as may be properly brought before the special
meeting or any adjournment or postponement thereof. Please refer to the accompanying proxy statement for further information with
respect to the business to be transacted at the special meeting.

In the materials accompanying this letter, you will find a Notice of Special Meeting of Stockholders, a proxy statement relating to
the actions to be taken by our stockholders at the special meeting and a proxy card. The proxy statement includes important
information about the merger agreement and the DTS merger. We encourage you to carefully read the entire proxy statement and its
annexes, including the merger agreement.

shares as soon as possible to make sure your shares are represented at the special meeting. Your failure to vote will have the
same effect as voting against the merger proposal.
 

Sincerely,

JON E. KIRCHNER
Chairman of the Board

This accompanying proxy statement is dated October 21, 2016, and is first being mailed or otherwise delivered to our
stockholders on or about October 24, 2016.

NOTICE OF SPECIAL MEETING OF STOCKHOLDERS
TO BE HELD ON DECEMBER 1, 2016

 
 

Dear Stockholder:

The board of directors of DTS, Inc. (“we,” “us,” “our” or “DTS”) has called for a special meeting of stockholders of DTS that
will be held at the Westlake Village Inn, 31943 Agoura Road, Westlake Village, California 91361, at 8:00 a.m., local time, on
December 1, 2016 (the “special meeting”) to consider and vote upon:
 

 
1. a proposal to adopt the Agreement and Plan of Merger, dated as of September 19, 2016 (the “merger agreement”), among

Tessera Technologies, Inc., DTS, Tempe Holdco Corporation, Tempe Merger Sub Corporation and Arizona Merger Sub
Corporation (the “merger proposal”);

 

 
2. a proposal to approve, on a non-binding, advisory basis, merger-related compensation for DTS’s named executive officers

(the “merger-related compensation proposal”); and
 

 
3. a proposal to adjourn the special meeting, if necessary or appropriate, to solicit additional proxies if there are not sufficient

votes at the time of the special meeting to approve the merger proposal (the “adjournment proposal”).

THE DTS BOARD OF DIRECTORS UNANIMOUSLY RECOMMENDS THAT DTS STOCKHOLDERS VOTE “FOR” THE
MERGER PROPOSAL, “FOR” THE MERGER-RELATED COMPENSATION PROPOSAL AND “FOR” THE
ADJOURNMENT PROPOSAL.

Record holders of DTS common stock at the close of business on October 20, 2016 will be entitled to vote at, or any adjournment
or postponement of, the special meeting. At least ten days prior to the special meeting, a complete list of stockholders of record as of
October 20, 2016 will be available for inspection by any stockholder for any purpose germane to the special meeting, during ordinary
business hours, at the office of the Secretary of DTS at 5220 Las Virgenes Road, Calabasas, California 91302. As a stockholder of
record, you are cordially invited to attend the special meeting in person. Regardless of whether you expect to be present at the special
meeting, please either complete, sign and date the enclosed proxy card and mail it promptly in the enclosed envelope, or vote
electronically via the Internet or telephone as described in greater detail in the proxy statement and on the enclosed proxy card.
Returning the enclosed proxy card, or voting electronically or telephonically, will not affect your right to vote in person if you attend
the special meeting.

Your vote is very important, regardless of the number of shares you own. Even if you plan to attend the special meeting in
person, we request that you complete, sign, date and return your proxy card in the enclosed envelope, or appoint a proxy over the
Internet or by telephone as instructed in these materials, to ensure that your shares will be represented at the special meeting if you are
unable to attend. If you sign, date and mail your proxy card or appoint a proxy over the Internet or by telephone without indicating how
you wish to vote, your shares will be voted for each of the merger proposal, the merger-related compensation proposal and the
adjournment proposal.

If you fail to return your proxy card fail to appoint a proxy over the Internet or by telephone and you do not attend the special
meeting, your shares will not be counted for purposes of determining whether a quorum is present at the special meeting and will have
the same effect as a vote against the merger proposal. If you do attend the special meeting and wish to vote in person, you may
withdraw your proxy appointment and vote in

QUESTIONS AND ANSWERS

The following questions and answers are intended to address some commonly asked questions regarding the DTS merger and the
special meeting. These questions and answers may not address all questions that may be important to you as a stockholder. To better
understand these matters, and for a description of the legal terms governing the DTS merger, you should carefully read this entire
proxy statement, including the annexes, as well as the documents that have been incorporated by reference in this proxy statement. See
“Where You Can Find More Information” beginning on page 96. All references in this proxy statement to “we,” “us,” our,” or “DTS”
refer to DTS, Inc., a Delaware corporation; all references in this proxy statement to “Tessera” refer to Tessera Technologies, Inc., a
Delaware corporation; all references in this proxy statement to “Holdco” refer to Tempe Holdco Corporation, a Delaware corporation
and a direct wholly owned subsidiary of Tessera; all references in this proxy statement to “Parent Merger Sub” refer to Tempe Merger
Sub Corporation, a Delaware corporation and a direct wholly owned subsidiary of Holdco; all references in this proxy statement to
“Company Merger Sub” refer to Arizona Merger Sub Corporation, a Delaware corporation and a direct wholly owned subsidiary of
Holdco; all references in this proxy statement to the “Merger Subs” refer to the Parent Merger Sub and the Company Merger Sub,
collectively; all references in this proxy statement to the “Parent Parties” refer to Tessera, Holdco and the Merger Subs, collectively;
all references in this proxy statement to the “closing date” refer to the date upon which the DTS merger occurs; all references to the
“merger agreement” refer to the Agreement and Plan of Merger, dated as of September 19, 2016, as it may be amended from time to
time, by and among Tessera, DTS, Holdco, Parent Merger Sub and Company Merger Sub, a copy of which is attached as Annex A to
this proxy statement; all references in this proxy statement to the “Parent merger” refer to the merger of Parent Merger Sub with and
into Tessera pursuant to the merger agreement; all references in this proxy statement to the “DTS merger” refer to the merger of
Company Merger Sub with and into DTS pursuant to the merger agreement; and all references in this proxy statement to the
“mergers” refer to the Parent merger and the DTS merger, collectively.

Questions and Answers About the DTS Merger
 

 Q: Why am I receiving this proxy statement?
 

 

A: On September 19, 2016, DTS entered into the Agreement and Plan of Merger, dated as of September 19, 2016 (the “merger
agreement”), among Tessera, DTS, Holdco, Parent Merger Sub and Company Merger Sub (the “merger agreement”).
Pursuant to the merger agreement, Company Merger Sub will be merged with and into DTS (the “DTS merger”). As a result
of the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, DTS stockholders will cease to own shares in DTS and will be
entitled to receive the merger consideration in exchange for their shares. The date upon which the DTS merger occurs is
referred to as the “closing date.”

DTS is holding a special meeting of stockholders (the “special meeting”) in order to obtain the stockholder approval
necessary to adopt the merger agreement (the “merger proposal”). DTS stockholders will also be asked to approve, on a
non-binding, advisory basis, merger-related compensation for DTS’s named executive officers (the “merger-related
compensation proposal”) and to adjourn the special meeting, if necessary or appropriate, to solicit additional proxies if there
are not sufficient votes at the time of the special meeting to approve the merger proposal (the “adjournment proposal”). DTS
will be unable to complete the DTS merger unless the DTS stockholders approve the merger proposal at the special meeting.

We have included in this proxy statement important information about the DTS merger, the merger agreement (a copy of
which is attached as Annex A) and the special meeting. You should read this information carefully and in its entirety. The
enclosed voting materials allow you to vote your shares without attending the special meeting. Your vote is very important
and we encourage you to submit your proxy as soon as possible.

 Q: Why is DTS conducting the DTS merger?
 

 

A: After careful consideration and consultation, the board of directors of DTS (the “DTS Board”) has determined that the DTS
merger and the other transactions contemplated by the merger agreement are in the best interests of DTS stockholders based
upon numerous factors that are described more fully under the section entitled “The DTS Merger—Recommendation of the
DTS Board; Reasons for the DTS Merger,” beginning on page 39. The DTS Board believes that the DTS merger presents the
best value available to DTS stockholders at this time.

 
 Q: What are the positive and negative factors that the DTS Board considered in connection with the DTS merger?
 

 

A: In evaluating the merger agreement and the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, including the DTS merger,
the DTS Board consulted with DTS management, its financial advisor and outside legal counsel. In recommending that
stockholders vote in favor of adoption of the merger agreement, the DTS Board considered a number of positive factors,
including the following (which factors are not necessarily exhaustive or presented in order of relative importance):

 

 
•  the all-cash nature of the consideration that DTS stockholders will be entitled to receive in connection with the DTS

merger, which allows DTS stockholders to realize immediate value, in cash, for their investment in DTS, while
enabling stockholders to avoid further risk of investment in DTS;

 

 
•  the relationship of the $42.50 per share consideration to the historical trading price of DTS common stock, par value

$0.0001 per share (“DTS common stock”);
 

 
•  the fact that DTS, together with management and its financial advisor, contacted several potential acquirors regarding

a sale of DTS;
 

 

•  the opinion of Centerview rendered to the DTS Board on September 19, 2016, which was subsequently confirmed by
delivery of a written opinion dated such date that, as of such date and based upon and subject to the assumptions
made, procedures followed, matters considered, and qualifications and limitations upon the review undertaken by
Centerview in preparing its opinion, the merger consideration to be paid to the holders of Shares (other than certain
shares excluded as specified in such opinion) pursuant to the merger agreement was fair, from a financial point of
view, to such holders, as more fully described under the caption “The DTS Merger—Opinion of Centerview Partners
LLC;” beginning on page 46;

 

 •  the terms of the merger agreement;
 

 
•  the DTS Board’s analysis of DTS’s background, recent operating history and current position in the marketplace in its

deliberations concerning the DTS merger and the other transactions contemplated by the merger agreement;
 

 •  the perceived risks and benefits of a variety of strategic alternatives for DTS;
 

 

•  the DTS Board’s consideration that DTS has explored various alternatives to an acquisition by Tessera, including
those described immediately above, and that such alternatives were not reasonably likely to create greater value for
DTS’s stockholders than the transaction with Tessera, taking into account execution risk as well as business,
competitive, industry and market risk;

 

 
•  the DTS Board’s belief that it had negotiated the highest price per share for DTS common stock that Tessera was

willing to pay, which negotiations are more fully described under the caption “The DTS Merger—Background of the
DTS Merger;” and

 

 
•  the DTS Board’s view that the terms of the merger agreement would be unlikely to deter interested third parties from

making a superior proposal, including the merger agreement’s terms and conditions as they relate to the DTS Board’s
ability to change its recommendation with

 
2



8/19/2019 DEFM14A

https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1226308/000119312516744017/d215313ddefm14a.htm 12/256

Table of Contents

 
respect to the DTS merger and the belief that the termination fee potentially payable to Tessera is reasonable in light
of the circumstances, consistent with comparable transactions and not preclusive of other offers.

The DTS Board also considered a number of uncertainties, risks and potentially negative factors in its deliberations
concerning the DTS merger, including the following (which factors are not necessarily exhaustive or presented in order of
relative importance):

 

 
•  the risks and costs to DTS if the DTS merger does not close, including the potential effect on DTS’s business and

relationships with customers, as well as the potential effect of the resulting public announcement of the termination of
the merger agreement on the trading price of DTS common stock;

 

 
•  the fact that the announcement and pendency of the DTS merger, or the failure to complete the DTS merger, may

cause substantial harm to DTS’s relationships with its employees, vendors and customers and may divert employees’
attention away from DTS’s day-to-day business operations;

 

 

•  the fact that DTS’s stockholders will receive the per share merger consideration in cash and will no longer have the
opportunity to participate in any future earnings or growth of DTS or benefit from any potential future appreciation in
the value of DTS shares, including any value that could be achieved if DTS engages in future strategic or other
transactions;

 

 

•  the fact that, subject to the terms and conditions of the merger agreement, DTS cannot solicit other acquisition
proposals, which could reduce the likelihood that other potential acquirers would propose an alternative transaction
that may be more advantageous to DTS’s stockholders, and must pay Tessera a termination fee of $25,500,000 under
certain circumstances following termination of the merger agreement, including if the DTS Board desires to terminate
the merger agreement to accept a superior proposal;

 

 •  the restrictions on the conduct of DTS’s business prior to the consummation of the DTS merger;
 

 
•  the fact that an all cash transaction would be taxable to DTS’s stockholders that are U.S. persons for U.S. federal

income tax purposes;
 

 
•  the significant costs involved in connection with entering into the merger agreement and completing the DTS merger

and the substantial time and effort of DTS management required to complete the DTS merger, which may disrupt
DTS’s business operations;

 

 
•  the fact that Tessera requires substantial third party debt financing for the transaction, and in the event that such third

party financing is not available to Tessera, Tessera may not have the financial resources to consummate the DTS
Merger; and

 

 
•  the fact that DTS’s directors and officers may have interests in the DTS merger that may be different from, or in

addition to, those of DTS’s other stockholders (see “The DTS Merger—Interests of DTS’s Directors and Executive
Officers in the DTS Merger”).

These factors are not necessarily exhaustive or presented in order of relative importance. Additional discussion about the
factors considered by the DTS Board with respect to the merger agreement and the transactions contemplated by the merger
agreement, including the DTS merger, can be found under the section entitled “The DTS Merger—Recommendation of the
DTS Board; Reasons for the DTS Merger,” beginning on page 39.

 
 Q: What will happen to DTS as a result of the DTS merger?
 

 
A: As a result of the DTS merger, DTS will become a wholly owned subsidiary of Holdco and its shares will no longer be listed

on the NASDAQ Global Select Market. Following consummation of the DTS merger, you will no longer have any interest in
DTS’s future earnings or growth, and the registration of

 
3



8/19/2019 DEFM14A

https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1226308/000119312516744017/d215313ddefm14a.htm 13/256

Table of Contents

 
DTS’s common stock and its reporting obligations with respect to its common stock under the Securities Exchange Act of
1934, as amended (the “Exchange Act”), will be terminated upon application to the Securities and Exchange Commission
(the “SEC”).

 
 Q: What will DTS stockholders receive in the DTS merger?
 

 

A: At the effective time of the DTS merger, each share of DTS common stock, will be converted into the right to receive $42.50
in cash, without interest and less any required tax withholdings (the “merger consideration”). All shares of DTS common
stock issued and outstanding that are held by Tessera or Holdco, or any of their respective subsidiaries or held by DTS as
treasury stock, or that are owned by DTS, Company Merger Sub or any wholly owned subsidiary of DTS and shares with
respect to which appraisal rights are properly exercised and not withdrawn (collectively, the “excluded shares”), will not be
converted into the right to receive the merger consideration and will be canceled. Holders of excluded shares with respect to
which appraisal rights are properly exercised and not withdrawn will have the right to obtain payment in cash for the fair
value of their shares of DTS common stock, as determined by the Delaware Court of Chancery, rather than the merger
consideration. The procedures to exercise appraisal rights are summarized under the section entitled “The DTS Merger—
Appraisal Rights” beginning on page 60, and the text of the applicable appraisal rights provisions of the Delaware General
Corporation Law (the “DGCL”) is included as Annex C to this proxy statement.

 
 

Q: How does the merger consideration compare to the market price of DTS common stock prior to the date on which the
merger agreement was publicly announced?

 

 

A: The merger consideration represents a premium of (i) approximately 24% to the per share closing price of DTS common
stock on September 19, 2016, the last trading day prior to the date on which the execution of the merger agreement was
publicly announced, (ii) approximately 26% to the volume weighted average share price of DTS common stock during the
thirty (30) days ended September 19, 2016 and (iii) approximately 24% to the high per share closing price of DTS common
stock during the 52 weeks ended September 19, 2016.

 
 Q: What conditions must be satisfied to complete the DTS merger?
 

 

A: The completion of the DTS merger depends on the satisfaction or waiver of a number of conditions, all of which, to the
extent permitted by applicable law, may be waived by DTS and/or Tessera, subject to the terms and conditions of the merger
agreement. These conditions include, among others: (i) the expiration or termination of the waiting period (and any
extensions of the waiting period) under the United States Hart-Scott-Rodino Antitrust Improvements Act of 1976 (the “HSR
Act”); (ii) the absence of any injunctions or any other legal order prohibiting or restraining the DTS merger; (iii) the
adoption of the merger agreement by DTS’s stockholders; (iv) subject to certain exceptions, the accuracy of DTS’s and
Tessera’s respective representations and warranties in the merger agreement; (v) performance by DTS and Tessera of their
respective obligations, covenants and agreements contained in the merger agreement; and (vi) the absence of any material
adverse effect on DTS. For a more complete summary of the conditions that must be satisfied or waived prior to completion
of the DTS merger, see “The Merger Agreement—Conditions to the Completion of the DTS Merger” beginning on page 86.

 
 

Q: Do any of the DTS directors or executive officers have interests in the DTS merger that may differ from those of
stockholders generally?

 

 
A: In considering the recommendations of the DTS Board, you should know that DTS’s directors and executive officers may

have interests in the DTS merger that may be different from, or in addition to, the interests of DTS’s stockholders generally.
The DTS Board was aware of and considered these

interests, among other matters, in evaluating and overseeing the negotiation of the merger agreement, in approving the

of DTS’s Directors and Executive Officers in the DTS Merger” beginning on page 53.

 
 Q: What constitutes a quorum?
 

 

A: A quorum will be present at the special meeting if a majority of the shares of DTS common stock issued and outstanding and
entitled to vote at the special meeting are present in person or represented by proxy. In the event that a quorum is not present
at the special meeting, or there are not sufficient votes at the time of the special meeting to approve the merger agreement, it
is expected that the special meeting will be adjourned to solicit additional proxies.

 
 Q: What vote is required to approve each proposal?
 

 

A: Required vote to approve the merger proposal: Approval of the merger proposal requires the affirmative vote of the holders
of a majority of the outstanding shares of DTS common stock entitled to vote in person or by proxy at the special meeting.
Accordingly, a DTS stockholder’s failure to vote, vote to abstain or failure to instruct his or her broker or nominee to vote
will have the same effect as a vote “AGAINST” the merger proposal.

Required vote to approve the merger-related compensation proposal: Approval of the non-binding, advisory merger-related
compensation proposal requires the affirmative vote of the holders of a majority of the total number of votes of DTS
common stock represented at the special meeting and entitled to vote on such proposal. Accordingly, a DTS stockholder’s
failure to vote or failure to instruct his or her broker or nominee to vote will have no effect on the merger-related
compensation proposal; however, a DTS stockholder’s vote to abstain will have the same effect as a vote “AGAINST” the
merger-related compensation proposal.

Required vote to approve the adjournment proposal: Approval of the adjournment proposal requires the affirmative vote of
the holders of a majority of the total number of votes of DTS common stock represented at the special meeting and entitled
to vote on such proposal. Accordingly, a DTS stockholder’s failure to vote or failure to instruct his or her broker or nominee
to vote will have no effect on the adjournment proposal, assuming a quorum is present; however, a DTS stockholder’s vote
to abstain will have the same effect as a vote “AGAINST” the adjournment proposal.

 
 Q: What are the recommendations of the DTS Board?
 

 

A: At a duly convened meeting held on September 19, 2016, the DTS Board unanimously (i) approved the merger agreement
and consummation of the DTS merger upon the terms and subject to the conditions set forth in the merger agreement, (ii)
determined that the terms of the merger agreement and the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, including the
DTS merger, are fair to, advisable and in the best interests of DTS and its stockholders, (iii) directed that the merger
agreement be submitted to DTS stockholders for adoption at the special meeting and (iv) recommended that DTS
stockholders adopt the merger agreement and approve the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, including the
DTS merger.

The DTS Board unanimously recommends that DTS stockholders vote “FOR” the merger proposal, “FOR” the
merger-related compensation proposal and “FOR” the adjournment proposal. See “The DTS Merger—
Recommendation of the DTS Board; Reasons for the DTS Merger” beginning on page 39.

 Q: When do you expect the DTS merger to be completed?
 

 

A: We anticipate that the DTS merger will be completed late in the fourth quarter of 2016 or early first quarter of 2017, but we
cannot predict the exact timing. In addition to obtaining the necessary DTS stockholder approval, all other conditions to the
DTS merger must be satisfied or waived. We cannot assure you that all conditions to the DTS merger will be satisfied or, if
satisfied, the date by which they will be satisfied.

 
 Q: What will happen to DTS stock options and other stock-based awards in the DTS merger?
 

 
A: For information concerning the treatment of DTS stock options and other stock-based awards, refer to the section entitled

“The Merger Agreement—Treatment of DTS Stock Options and Other Stock-Based Awards” beginning on page 73.

 
 Q: Is the DTS merger expected to be taxable to U.S. persons?
 

 
A: Yes. The exchange of shares of our common stock for the merger consideration of $42.50 in cash pursuant to the DTS

merger will generally be a taxable transaction to U.S. persons (as defined under the caption “The DTS Merger—Material
U.S. Federal Income Tax Consequences of the DTS Merger” beginning on page 64) for U.S. federal income tax purposes.

If you are a U.S. person and you exchange your shares of our common stock in the DTS merger for cash, you will generally
recognize gain or loss in an amount equal to the difference, if any, between the amount of cash received with respect to such
shares and your adjusted tax basis in such shares of our common stock. Backup withholding may also apply to the cash
payments paid to a non-corporate U.S. person pursuant to the DTS merger unless the U.S. person or other payee provides a
taxpayer identification number, certifies that such number is correct and otherwise complies with the backup withholding
rules. We encourage you to read “Material U.S. Federal Income Tax Consequences of the DTS Merger” for a more detailed
discussion of the U.S. federal income tax consequences of the DTS merger. You should also consult your tax advisor for a
complete analysis of the effect of the DTS merger on your federal, state and local and/or foreign taxes.

Please see “The DTS Merger—Material U.S. Federal Income Tax Consequences of the DTS Merger” beginning on page 64
for more information concerning the withholding of taxes from the merger consideration.

 
 Q: Are stockholders entitled to appraisal rights?
 

 

A: Under Delaware law, holders of shares of DTS common stock that meet certain requirements and follow certain procedures
under Delaware law will have the right to obtain payment in cash for the fair value of their shares of DTS common stock, as
determined by the Delaware Court of Chancery, rather than the merger consideration. Appraisal rights are only available to
stockholders who do not vote in favor of adopting the merger agreement, and a vote in favor of adopting the merger
agreement will constitute a waiver of a stockholder’s appraisal rights. To exercise appraisal rights, stockholders must strictly
follow the procedures prescribed by Delaware law. These procedures are summarized under the section entitled “The DTS
Merger—Appraisal Rights” beginning on page 60. In addition, the text of the applicable appraisal rights provisions of
Delaware law is included as Annex C to this proxy statement.

 
 Q: What happens if the DTS merger is not consummated?
 

 
A: If the merger agreement is not adopted by our stockholders or if the DTS merger is not consummated for any other reason,

stockholders will not be entitled to receive any payment for their shares of DTS

8/19/2019 DEFM14A

common stock in connection with the DTS merger. Instead, DTS will remain a public company and DTS common stock will
continue to be listed and traded on the NASDAQ Global Select Market. Under specified circumstances, DTS may be
required to pay Tessera a fee with respect to the termination of the merger agreement, as described under “The Merger
Agreement—Termination Fees; Expenses” beginning on page 89.

 
 

Q: If the DTS merger is completed, when can I expect to receive the merger consideration for my shares of DTS common
stock?

 

 

A: After the DTS merger is consummated, you will receive written instructions for exchanging your shares of DTS common
stock for the merger consideration. Please do not return stock certificates with the enclosed proxy card. The conversion of
your shares of DTS common stock into the right to receive $42.50 in cash, without interest and less any required tax
withholdings, will occur automatically at the effective time of the DTS merger. Within five business days after the effective
time of the DTS merger, the payment agent, which will be selected by Tessera on or prior to the closing date, will mail to
each holder of record whose shares of DTS common stock were converted into the right to receive the merger consideration,
a letter of transmittal in customary form, accompanied by instructions for surrendering DTS stock certificates or transferring
DTS book entry shares, as applicable, in exchange for the DTS merger consideration. Upon surrender of your DTS
certificate to the payment agent for exchange or receipt of an “agent’s message” by the payment agent (in the case of book
entry shares), in each case together with a duly completed and validly executed letter of transmittal, you will be entitled to
receive, without interest and less any required tax withholdings, the merger consideration, and your certificate or book entry
shares so surrendered will be canceled.

 
 Q: What happens if I sell my shares of common stock before the special meeting?
 

 

A: The record date for the special meeting is earlier than the date of the special meeting and the date that the DTS merger is
expected to be completed. If you transfer your shares after the applicable record date, but before the special meeting, unless
the transferee receives your proxy, you will retain your right to vote at such special meeting, but will have transferred the
right to receive the merger consideration in the DTS merger. In order to receive the merger consideration you must hold your
shares of DTS common stock through completion of the DTS merger.

 
 

Q: What happens if I sell my shares of common stock after the special meeting, but before the effective time of the DTS
merger?

 

 
A: If you transfer your shares after the special meeting, but before the effective time of the DTS merger, you will have

transferred the right to receive the merger consideration in the DTS merger. In order to receive the merger consideration, you
must hold your shares of DTS common stock through completion of the DTS merger.

Questions and Answers About the Special Meeting
 

 Q: When and where will the special meeting be held?
 

 
A: The special meeting will be held at the Westlake Village Inn, 31943 Agoura Road, Westlake Village, California 91361 on

December 1, 2016, at 8:00 a.m., Pacific time, unless the special meeting is adjourned or postponed.

 
 Q: Who is entitled to vote at the special meeting?
 

 
A: DTS has fixed October 20, 2016 as the record date for the special meeting. If you were a DTS stockholder at the close of

business on such date, you are entitled to vote on matters that come before the special meeting. However, a stockholder may
only vote his or her shares if he or she is present in person or is represented by proxy at the special meeting.

Table of Contents

 Q: How many votes do I have?
 

 A: Stockholders are entitled to one vote at the special meeting for each share of DTS common stock held as of the record date.

 
 Q: My shares are held in “street name” by my broker. Will my broker automatically vote my shares for me?
 

 

A: No. If your shares are held in “street name” by your bank, broker or other nominee, and you do not provide voting
instructions to your bank, broker or other nominee on a particular proposal on which such bank, broker or nominee does not
have discretionary authority to vote, your shares will not be voted on that proposal. This is called a “broker non-vote.” A
broker non-vote will have the same effect as a vote “AGAINST” the merger proposal and will have no effect on the merger-
related compensation proposal or the adjournment proposal.

 
 Q: What do I need to do now?
 

 
A: Read and consider the information contained in this proxy statement, including the annexes hereto and any documents

incorporated herein by reference, carefully, and then please vote your shares as soon as possible so that your shares may be
represented at your special meeting.

 
 Q: How do I vote?
 

 

A: Even if you plan to attend the special meeting, we encourage you to vote your shares by proxy as soon as possible. After
carefully reading and considering the information contained in this proxy statement, please submit your proxy by telephone
or over the Internet in accordance with the instructions set forth on the enclosed proxy card, or mark, sign and date the proxy
card, and return it in the enclosed postage-paid envelope as soon as possible so that your shares may be voted at the special
meeting. For detailed information, see “The Special Meeting” beginning on page 22. YOUR VOTE IS VERY IMPORTANT.

 
 Q: As a participant in the DTS employee stock purchase plan, how do I vote shares held in my plan account?
 

 
A: Shares of common stock purchased through the DTS, Inc. 2013 Amended and Restated Employee Stock Purchase Plan and

the DTS, Inc. 2013 Amended and Restated Foreign Subsidiary Employee Stock Purchase Plan are held in brokerage
accounts and are treated the same as other beneficially owned shares.

 
 

Q: Can I change my vote after I have submitted a proxy by telephone or over the Internet or submitted my completed
proxy card?

 

 

A: Yes. You can change your vote by revoking your proxy at any time before it is voted at the special meeting. You can do this
in one of four ways: (1) appoint a proxy again by telephone or through the Internet; (2) submit another properly completed
proxy card with a later date; (3) attend the special meeting and vote in person; or (4) send a timely written notice of
revocation to the Corporate Secretary of DTS. Please note that to be effective, your new proxy card, Internet or telephonic
voting instructions or written notice of revocation must be received by the Corporate Secretary prior to the special meeting
and, in the case of Internet or telephonic voting instructions, must be received by 11:59 p.m., Eastern time, on November 30,
2016.

If you have instructed a broker to vote your shares, you must follow directions received from your broker to change your
vote.

SUMMARY

The following summary highlights selected information from this proxy statement and may not contain all of the
information that may be important to you. For a more complete description of the transactions contemplated by the merger
agreement, including the DTS merger, stockholders are encouraged to carefully read this entire proxy statement, its
annexes and the documents referred to or incorporated by reference in this proxy statement. Each item in this summary
includes a page reference directing you to a more complete description of that item. Please see the section entitled “Where
You Can Find More Information” beginning on page 96. This summary and the rest of this document contain forward-
looking statements about events that are not certain to occur, and you should not rely on those statements; see the section
entitled “Special Note Regarding Forward-Looking Statements” beginning on page 19 for more information.

The Merger Agreement and the DTS Merger (Page 68)

DTS has agreed to be acquired by Tessera pursuant to the merger agreement in a transaction that will result in DTS becoming
a wholly owned subsidiary of Holdco. In the DTS merger, Company Merger Sub will merge with and into DTS, with DTS
continuing as the surviving corporation and as a wholly owned subsidiary of Holdco. As a result of the DTS merger, DTS will
cease to be a publicly-traded company. Following consummation of the DTS merger, you will no longer have any interest in DTS’s
future earnings or growth and the registration of DTS common stock and DTS’s reporting obligations with respect to DTS common
stock under the Exchange Act will be terminated upon application to the SEC. In addition, following consummation of the DTS
merger, shares of DTS common stock will no longer be listed on any stock exchange, including the NASDAQ Global Select
Market. The merger agreement is attached as Annex A to this proxy statement. We encourage you to read this document in its
entirety; it is the principal document governing the DTS merger and other related transactions.

Parties to the Merger Agreement (Page 21)

DTS

DTS, Inc., a Delaware corporation, is a premier audio solutions provider for high-definition entertainment experiences. DTS’s
principal executive offices are located at 5220 Las Virgenes Road, Calabasas, California, 91302. DTS’s telephone number is (818)
436-1000 and its web site is www.dts.com. DTS common stock is publicly traded on the NASDAQ Global Select Market under the
ticker symbol “DTSI.”

Tessera

Tessera Technologies, Inc., a Delaware corporation, licenses its technologies and intellectual property to customers for use in
areas such as mobile computing and communications, memory and data storage, and 3-D Integrated Circuit technologies, among
others. Tessera’s principal executive offices are located at 3025 Orchard Parkway, San Jose, California 95134. Tessera’s telephone
number is (408) 321-6000 and its web site is www.tessera.com. Tessera’s common stock is publicly traded on the NASDAQ
Global Select Market under the ticker symbol “TSRA.”

Holdco

Tempe Holdco Corporation is a Delaware corporation and a direct wholly owned subsidiary of Tessera. Holdco was
incorporated on September 15, 2016 solely for the purpose of effecting the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement.
From the date of incorporation to date, Holdco has not conducted any activities other than those incident to its formation and the
taking of certain steps in connection with the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement. Holdco’s principal executive
offices are located at 3025 Orchard Parkway, San Jose, California 95134 and its telephone number is (408) 321-6000.

Merger Consideration (Page 72)

At the effective time of the DTS merger, each outstanding share of DTS common stock, other than the excluded shares (as
defined on page 4), will be converted into the right to receive $42.50 in cash, without interest and less any required tax
withholdings (the “merger consideration”).

Treatment of DTS Stock Options and Other Stock-Based Awards (Page 73)

Upon completion of the DTS merger, each then-outstanding (i) in-the-money, vested DTS stock option and vested DTS
service-based restricted stock unit (each, a “DTS RSU”) will be canceled, and the holder of such stock option or restricted stock
unit, as applicable, will be entitled to receive cash as set forth in the merger agreement and (ii) DTS performance-based restricted
stock unit (each, a “DTS PRSU”) (treating for this purpose any performance-based vesting condition to which such performance-
based restricted stock unit is subject as of the effective time of the DTS merger or was as of the date of the merger agreement as
having been attained at the “target level”) will become fully vested and canceled, and the holder of such performance-based
restricted stock unit will be entitled to receive cash as set forth in the merger agreement.

Upon completion of the DTS merger, each then-outstanding (i) out-of-the-money, vested or unvested DTS stock option and
in-the-money, unvested DTS stock option will be assumed by Holdco and converted into a stock option to purchase shares of
Holdco common stock pursuant to the exchange ratio set forth in the merger agreement and (ii) unvested DTS service-based
restricted stock unit will be assumed by Holdco and converted into a Holdco service-based restricted stock unit pursuant to the
exchange ratio set forth in the merger agreement.

The special meeting is scheduled to be held at the Westlake Village Inn, 31943 Agoura Road, Westlake Village, California
91361 on December 1, at 8:00 a.m., Pacific time, unless the special meeting is adjourned or postponed. At the special meeting,
stockholders will be asked to consider and vote upon the following matters: (i) the merger proposal; (ii) the merger-related
compensation proposal; and (iii) the adjournment proposal. Only holders of record of shares of DTS common stock at the close of
business on October 20, 2016, the record date for the special meeting, are entitled to notice of and to vote at the time of the special
meeting or any postponements or adjournments thereof. See “The Special Meeting” for additional information on the special
meeting, including details regarding proxy and voting procedures.

Vote Required (Page 23)

Merger Proposal: Approval of the merger proposal requires the affirmative vote of holders of a majority of the shares of DTS
common stock outstanding and entitled to vote. Accordingly, a stockholder’s failure to submit a proxy card or to vote in
person at the special meeting, an abstention from voting, or the failure of a stockholder who holds his or her shares in
“street name” through a broker or other nominee to give voting instructions to such broker or other nominee, will have the
same effect as a vote “AGAINST” the proposal to adopt the merger agreement.

Merger-Related Compensation Proposal: Approval of the non-binding, advisory merger-related compensation proposal
requires the affirmative vote of holders of a majority of the shares of DTS common stock present, in person or represented by
proxy, at the special meeting and entitled to vote on the merger-related compensation proposal. Accordingly, abstentions will
have the same effect as a vote “AGAINST” the merger-related compensation proposal, while broker non-votes and shares
not in attendance at the special meeting will have no effect on the outcome of any vote to approve the merger-related
compensation proposal.

Adjournment Proposal: Approval of the adjournment proposal requires the affirmative vote of holders of a majority of the
shares of DTS common stock present, in person or represented by proxy, at the special meeting and entitled to vote on the
adjournment proposal. Accordingly, abstentions will have the same effect as a vote “AGAINST” the adjournment proposal,
while broker non-votes and shares not in attendance at the special meeting will have no effect on the outcome of any vote to
adjourn the special meeting.

Recommendation of the DTS Board (Page 39)

At a duly convened meeting held on September 19, 2016, the DTS Board unanimously (i) approved the merger agreement and
consummation of the DTS merger upon the terms and subject to the conditions set forth in the merger agreement, (ii) determined
that the terms of the merger agreement and the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, including the DTS merger, are
fair to, advisable and in the best interests of DTS and its stockholders, (iii) directed that the merger agreement be submitted to DTS
stockholders for adoption at the special meeting and (iv) recommended that DTS stockholders adopt the merger agreement and
approve the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, including the DTS merger. Accordingly, the DTS Board
unanimously recommends that DTS stockholders vote “FOR” the merger proposal, “FOR” the merger-related
compensation proposal and “FOR” the adjournment proposal.

merger, and in recommending that the merger agreement be adopted by the stockholders of DTS.

Governmental Approvals (Page 66)

DTS and Tessera are not required to complete the DTS merger unless a number of regulatory conditions are satisfied or
waived. These conditions include: (i) the absence of any injunctions or any other legal order prohibiting or restraining the mergers
and (ii) the expiration or termination of the waiting period under the HSR Act.

Each of DTS, Tessera, Holdco, Parent Merger Sub and Company Merger Sub have agreed to use their reasonable best efforts
to take, or cause to be taken, all actions necessary, proper or advisable to comply promptly with all legal requirements which may
be imposed on such party or its subsidiaries with respect to the mergers, to consummate the transactions contemplated by the
merger agreement as promptly as practicable and to obtain (and to cooperate with the other party to obtain) any consent,
authorization, order or approval of, or any exemption by, any governmental entity or any other third party which is required in
connection with the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, and to comply with the terms and conditions of any such
consent, authorization, order or approval.

Table of Contents

Under the HSR Act and the rules and regulations promulgated thereunder, the DTS merger may not be consummated until the
expiration of a 30-calendar-day waiting period following the parties’ filing of their respective HSR Act notification forms or the
earlier termination of that waiting period. If the U.S. Department of Justice (the “DOJ”), or the Federal Trade Commission (the
“FTC”), issues a Request for Additional Information and Documentary Material (a “second request”) prior to the expiration of the
initial waiting period, the parties must observe a second 30-day waiting period, which would begin to run only after both parties
have substantially complied with the request for additional information, unless the waiting period is terminated earlier. DTS and
Tessera each filed the required HSR notification and report forms on October 3, 2016, commencing the initial 30-calendar-day
waiting period. The FTC granted early termination of the waiting period on October 17, 2016.

DTS cannot assure you that all of the regulatory approvals described above will be obtained and, if obtained, DTS cannot
assure you as to the timing of any approvals, the ability to obtain the approvals on satisfactory terms or the absence of any
litigation challenging such approvals.

Description of Financing (Page 67)

We anticipate that the total amount of cash necessary to complete the DTS merger and the related transactions will be
approximately $970,000,000, which will be funded with borrowings under the debt financing described below as well as cash on
hand of DTS and Tessera. This amount includes funds needed to (1) pay DTS stockholders the amounts due under the merger
agreement, (2) make payments in respect of outstanding DTS equity awards that are converted into the right to receive cash at
closing pursuant to the merger agreement, (3) repay existing indebtedness of DTS under its existing credit facility, (4) pay certain
transaction fees, including advisory fees and debt financing fees and (5) pay certain DTS employee bonus and change in control
payments.

In connection with the DTS merger, Tessera entered into a commitment letter (the “Debt Commitment Letter”), dated as of
September 19, 2016, as amended and restated on October 11, 2016, with Royal Bank of Canada (“RBC”), Bank of Montreal
(“BMO”) and BMO Capital Markets Corp. (“BMOCM”), pursuant to which, among other things, RBC and BMO, have committed
to provide a $600,000,000 senior secured term loan facility (the “Loan Facility”), subject to satisfaction of customary closing
conditions. The Loan Facility is available to (i) finance the acquisition of DTS, (ii) repay existing indebtedness of DTS under its
existing credit facility, and (iii) pay fees and expenses related thereto. Under the terms of the Debt Commitment Letter, RBC and
BMOCM will act as joint lead arrangers and joint bookrunning managers. The actual documentation governing the Loan Facility
has not been finalized, and accordingly, the actual terms may differ from the description of such terms in the Debt Commitment
Letter. The obligations of Tessera, Holdco, Parent Merger Sub and Company Merger Sub to consummate the mergers are not
subject to any financing condition.

No Solicitation (Page 80)

DTS has agreed not to solicit, initiate or knowingly take any action to facilitate or encourage any acquisition proposal or
proposal or inquiry that constitutes, or would reasonably be expected to lead to, an acquisition proposal. However, at any time prior
to the effective time of the DTS merger, under specific circumstances, DTS may provide information to, and participate in
discussions and negotiations with, third parties in response to an unsolicited written acquisition proposal that did not result from a
breach of DTS’s non-solicitation obligations under the merger agreement, and that constitutes or which is reasonably expected to
lead to a superior proposal, if the DTS Board determines in good faith, after consultation with legal counsel, that not taking such
action would reasonably be expected to constitute a breach of the DTS Board’s fiduciary duties under applicable law. DTS has also
agreed to promptly provide written notice to Tessera after receipt of any such acquisition proposal.

The merger agreement generally restricts the ability of the DTS Board from withdrawing or changing its recommendation in
favor of the DTS merger. However, the DTS Board may withdraw or change its recommendation (i) in circumstances not relating
to an acquisition proposal, if the DTS Board concludes in good

Conditions to the Completion of the DTS Merger (Page 86)

The completion of the DTS merger depends upon the satisfaction or waiver of a number of conditions, all of which, to the
extent permitted by applicable law, may be waived by DTS and/or Tessera, in accordance with the terms and conditions of the
merger agreement.

The following conditions must be satisfied or waived before either party is obligated to complete the DTS merger:
 

 •  the waiting period (and any extensions of the waiting period) under the HSR Act has expired or been terminated;
 

 
•  no law or order, writ, injunction, judgment, decree or ruling (whether temporary, preliminary or permanent) enacted,

promulgated, issued or entered by any governmental body of competent jurisdiction is in effect enjoining, restraining,
preventing or prohibiting the consummation of the mergers or making consummation of the mergers illegal; and

 

 
•  DTS has obtained the approval of its stockholders necessary to adopt the merger agreement (the “DTS stockholder

approval”).

•  the representations and warranties of the Parent Parties set forth in the merger agreement with respect to (i) due
authorization shall be true and correct in all material respects as of the date of the merger agreement and as of the
effective times of the mergers as if made at and as of such time and (ii) all other matters set forth in the merger
agreement shall be true and correct in all respects as of the date of

Termination (Page 87)

The merger agreement may be terminated and the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, including the DTS
merger, may be abandoned by written notice of the terminating party to the other parties:
 

 •  by mutual written consent of Tessera and DTS at any time prior to the receipt of the DTS stockholder approval;
 

 
•  by either Tessera or DTS if the DTS merger shall have not been consummated on or prior to 5:00 p.m., New York City

time, on February 28, 2017 (the “Outside Date”), subject to certain exceptions;
 

 
•  by either Tessera or DTS at any time prior to the receipt of the DTS stockholder approval if any final, non-appealable

legal restraint shall be in effect having the effect of making illegal, permanently restraining, enjoining or prohibiting the
consummation of the DTS merger;

 

 
•  by either Tessera or DTS if the DTS stockholder approval shall not have been obtained by reason of the failure to obtain

the required vote at a DTS stockholder meeting, subject to certain exceptions;
 

 •  by Tessera at any time prior to the receipt of the DTS stockholder approval if certain “triggering” events have occurred;
 

 

•  by Tessera if there has been a material breach of any covenant, obligation or agreement on the part of DTS or any
representation or warranty of DTS in the merger agreement shall have been inaccurate when made or, if not made as of a
specific date, shall have become inaccurate, that would result in certain conditions to the obligations of the Parent Parties
to effect the Parent merger not being satisfied, and such breach is not curable by the Outside Date, or, if curable through
the exercise of commercially reasonable efforts, is not cured within 15 business days of the date Tessera gives DTS
notice of such breach or inaccuracy, subject to certain exceptions;

 

 

•  by DTS if there has been a material breach of any covenant, obligation or agreement on the part of the Parent Parties or
any representation or warranty of the Parent Parties in the merger agreement shall have been inaccurate when made or, if
not made as of a specific date, shall have become inaccurate, that would result in certain conditions to the obligations of
DTS to effect the DTS merger not being satisfied, and such breach is not curable by the Outside Date, or, if curable
through the exercise of commercially reasonable efforts, is not cured within 15 business days of the date DTS gives
Tessera notice of such breach or inaccuracy, subject to certain exceptions;

 

 
•  by DTS at any time prior to the receipt of the DTS stockholder approval to enter into a definitive acquisition agreement

authorized by the DTS Board providing for a superior proposal and,

Effect of Termination (Page 88)

If the merger agreement is terminated as described above, the merger agreement will be of no further force or effect, except
for certain sections of the merger agreement. Such termination will not relieve any party to the merger agreement of any liability
for any fraud or the willful and material breach by any party of its representations, warranties, covenants, obligations or other
agreements set forth in the merger agreement.

Termination Fees; Expenses (Page 89)

All costs and expenses incurred in connection with the merger agreement are to be paid by the party incurring such fees and
expenses, unless otherwise set forth in the merger agreement.

The merger agreement provides that DTS will pay Tessera a cash termination fee of $25,500,000 (the “termination fee”),
under certain circumstances, which termination fee shall be made by wire transfer of immediately available funds as described
below:
 

 
•  in the event the merger agreement is terminated by Tessera at any time prior to the receipt of the DTS stockholder

approval if a “triggering event” shall have occurred, then DTS has agreed to pay to Tessera the termination fee no later
than the second business day following such termination;

 

 

•  in the event the merger agreement is terminated by either Tessera or DTS if the DTS stockholder approval shall not have
been obtained by reason of the failure to obtain the required vote at the special meeting, at any time after the occurrence
of any triggering event, then DTS has agreed to pay to Tessera the termination fee no later than the second business day
following such termination;

 

 

•  in the event the merger agreement is terminated by DTS at any time prior to the receipt of the DTS stockholder approval
to enter into a definitive acquisition agreement authorized by the DTS Board providing for a superior proposal and,
concurrently with such termination, DTS enters into such definitive acquisition agreement, and provided that DTS shall
have complied in all material respects with its non-solicitation obligations as described under “The Merger Agreement—
Covenants and Agreements—No Solicitation,” then DTS has agreed to pay to Tessera the termination fee concurrently
with such termination; and

 

 

•  if (i) after the date of the merger agreement, an acquisition proposal becomes publicly known or delivered to the DTS
Board and not publicly withdrawn, (ii) thereafter, the merger agreement is terminated (A) by Tessera or DTS under
certain termination provisions of the merger agreement and (iii) within 12 months after such termination DTS either
enters into a definitive agreement with respect to any acquisition proposal that is subsequently consummated or
consummates a transaction contemplated by any acquisition proposal, then DTS has agreed to pay to Tessera the
termination fee on the date DTS consummates such transaction.

DTS and the Parent Parties have acknowledged that the termination fee provisions of the merger agreement are an integral
part of the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement and that, without these agreements, DTS and the Parent Parties
would not have entered into the merger agreement. Notwithstanding the foregoing, in no event shall the full amount of the
termination fee be paid more than once and not in duplication even though the termination fee may be payable under one or more
provisions of the merger agreement.

Material U.S. Federal Income Tax Consequences of the DTS Merger (Page 64)

The exchange of shares of DTS common stock for cash in the DTS merger will generally be a taxable transaction to U.S.
persons (as defined in “The DTS Merger—Material U.S. Federal Income Tax Consequences of the DTS Merger”) for U.S. federal
income tax purposes, as well as under state and local and other tax laws. In general, a U.S. person (as defined in “Material U.S.
Federal Income Tax Consequences of the DTS Merger”) whose shares of DTS common stock are converted into the right to
receive cash in the merger will recognize gain or loss for U.S. federal income tax purposes in an amount equal to the difference, if
any, between the amount of cash received with respect to such shares and the U.S. person’s adjusted tax basis in such shares. You
are also encouraged to consult your own tax advisor regarding the U.S. federal income tax consequences of the mergers in your
particular circumstances, as well as tax consequences arising under the laws of any state, local or foreign taxing jurisdiction.

Appraisal Rights (Page 60)

Under Delaware law, holders of shares of DTS common stock that meet certain requirements and follow certain procedures
under Delaware law will have the right to obtain payment in cash for the fair value of their shares of DTS common stock, as
determined by the Delaware Court of Chancery, rather than the merger consideration. Appraisal rights are only available to
stockholders who do not vote in favor of adopting the merger agreement, and a vote in favor of adopting the merger agreement will
constitute a waiver of a stockholder’s appraisal rights. To exercise appraisal rights, stockholders must strictly follow the procedures
prescribed by Delaware law. These procedures are summarized under the section entitled “The DTS Merger—Appraisal Rights”
beginning on page 60. In addition, the text of the applicable appraisal rights provisions of Delaware law is included as Annex C to
this proxy statement.

PARTIES TO THE MERGER AGREEMENT

DTS

DTS, Inc., a Delaware corporation, is a premier audio solutions provider for high-definition entertainment experiences.
Headquartered in Calabasas, California, DTS’s audio solutions are designed to enable recording, delivery and playback of simple,
personalized, and immersive high-definition audio which are incorporated by hundreds of licensee customers around the world, into an
array of consumer electronics devices, including televisions (TVs), personal computers (PCs), smartphones, tablets, automotive audio
systems, digital media players, set-top-boxes, soundbars, wireless speakers, video game consoles, Blu-ray Disc players, audio/video
receivers, DVD-based products, and home theater systems. DTS’s principal executive offices are located at 5220 Las Virgenes Road,
Calabasas, California 91302, and its telephone number is (818) 436-1000. DTS’s website address is www.dts.com. The information
provided on DTS’s website is not part of this proxy statement and, therefore, is not incorporated herein by reference. DTS common
stock is publicly traded on the NASDAQ Global Select Market under the ticker symbol “DTSI.”

Tessera

Tessera Technologies, Inc., a Delaware corporation, licenses its technologies and intellectual property to customers for use in
areas such as mobile computing and communications, memory and data storage, and 3-D Integrated Circuit technologies, among
others. Tessera’s principal executive offices are located at 3025 Orchard Parkway, San Jose, California 95134. Tessera’s telephone
number is (408) 321-6000 and its web site is www.tessera.com. The information provided on Tessera’s website is not part of this proxy
statement and, therefore, is not incorporated herein by reference. Tessera’s common stock is publicly traded on the NASDAQ Global
Select Market under the ticker symbol “TSRA.”

Holdco

Tempe Holdco Corporation is a Delaware corporation and a direct wholly owned subsidiary of Tessera. Holdco was incorporated
on September 15, 2016 solely for the purpose of effecting the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement. From the date of
incorporation to date, Holdco has not conducted any activities other than those incident to its formation and the taking of certain steps
in connection with the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement. Holdco’s principal executive offices are located at 3025
Orchard Parkway, San Jose, California 95134 and its telephone number is (408) 321-6000.

Parent Merger Sub

Tempe Merger Sub Corporation is a Delaware corporation and a direct wholly owned subsidiary of Holdco. Parent Merger Sub
was incorporated on September 15, 2016 solely for the purpose of effecting the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement.
From the date of incorporation to date, Parent Merger Sub has not conducted any activities other than those incident to its formation
and the taking of certain steps in connection with the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement. Parent Merger Sub’s
principal executive offices are located at 3025 Orchard Parkway, San Jose, California 95134 and its telephone number is (408) 321-
6000.

Company Merger Sub

Arizona Merger Sub Corporation is a Delaware corporation and a direct wholly owned subsidiary of Holdco. Company Merger
Sub was incorporated on September 15, 2016 solely for the purpose of effecting the transactions contemplated by the merger
agreement. From the date of incorporation to date, Company Merger Sub has not conducted any activities other than those incident to
its formation and the taking of certain steps in connection with the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement. Company
Merger Sub’s principal executive offices are located at 3025 Orchard Parkway, San Jose, California 95134 and its telephone number is
(408) 321-6000.

THE SPECIAL MEETING

Your proxy is solicited on behalf of the DTS Board for use at the special meeting of stockholders to be held on December 1, 2016,
or at any adjournment or postponement thereof, for the purposes discussed in this proxy statement and in the accompanying Notice of
Special Meeting, and any other business properly brought before the special meeting. Proxies are solicited to give all stockholders of
record an opportunity to vote on matters properly presented at the special meeting. On or about October 24, 2016, we commenced
mailing this proxy statement and the enclosed form of proxy to our stockholders entitled to vote at the special meeting.

Date, Time and Place

The special meeting will be held at the Westlake Village Inn, 31943 Agoura Road, Westlake Village, California 91361, at
8:00 a.m., local time, on December 1, 2016, unless adjourned or postponed to a later date or time.

Purpose of the Special Meeting

At the special meeting, we are asking holders of record on October 20, 2016 to consider and vote on the following:
 

 •  a proposal to adopt the merger agreement (the “merger proposal”);
 

 
•  a proposal to approve, on a non-binding, advisory basis, merger-related compensation for DTS’s named executive officers

(the “merger-related compensation proposal”); and
 

 
•  a proposal to adjourn the special meeting, if necessary or appropriate, to solicit additional proxies if there are not sufficient

votes at the time of the special meeting to approve the merger proposal (the “adjournment proposal”).

At a duly convened meeting held September 19, 2016, the DTS Board unanimously (i) approved the merger agreement and
consummation of the DTS merger upon the terms and subject to the conditions set forth in the merger agreement, (ii) determined that
the terms of the merger agreement and the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, including the DTS merger, are fair to,
advisable and in the best interests of, DTS and its stockholders, (iii) directed that the merger agreement be submitted to DTS
stockholders for adoption at the special meeting and (iv) recommended that DTS stockholders adopt the merger agreement and approve
the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, including the DTS merger. Accordingly, the DTS Board unanimously
recommends that DTS stockholders vote “FOR” the merger proposal, “FOR” the merger-related compensation proposal and
“FOR” the adjournment proposal.

In considering the recommendation of the DTS Board, you should be aware that certain of DTS’s directors and executive officers
may have interests in the DTS merger that are different from, or in addition to, yours. The DTS Board was aware of and considered
these interests, among other matters, in evaluating the merger agreement and the transactions contemplated thereby, and in
recommending that the stockholders adopt the merger agreement and approve the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement,
including the DTS merger. See the section entitled “The DTS Merger—Interests of DTS’s Directors and Executive Officers in the DTS
Merger” beginning on page 53.

This proxy statement contains important information regarding these proposals and factors that DTS stockholders should consider
when deciding how to cast their votes. DTS stockholders are encouraged to read this entire document carefully, including the annexes
to and documents incorporated by reference into this document, for more detailed information regarding the merger agreement and the
transactions.

Record Date; Stock Entitled to Vote

Only holders of record of DTS common stock at the close of business on October 20, 2016, the record date for the special
meeting, are entitled to notice of and to vote at the special meeting or any postponements or
 

22



8/19/2019 DEFM14A

https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1226308/000119312516744017/d215313ddefm14a.htm 32/256

Table of Contents

adjournments thereof. For each share of DTS common stock you owned on the record date, you are entitled to cast one vote on each
matter voted upon at the special meeting. As of the record date, there were 17,848,590 shares of DTS common stock issued and
outstanding and entitled to vote at the special meeting.

Quorum and Vote Required

A quorum of stockholders is necessary to hold the special meeting. A quorum will be present at the special meeting if a majority
of the shares of DTS common stock issued and outstanding and entitled to vote at the special meeting are present in person or
represented by proxy. In the event that a quorum is not present at the special meeting, or there are not sufficient votes at the time of the
special meeting to approve the merger agreement, it is expected that the special meeting will be adjourned to solicit additional proxies.

Abstentions (shares of DTS common stock for which proxies have been received but for which the holders have abstained from
voting) count as shares present for establishing a quorum. Broker non-votes (shares of DTS common stock held by a bank, broker or
other nominee for the benefit of its client that are represented at the special meeting, but with respect to which such bank, broker or
other nominee is not instructed to vote on a particular proposal and does not have discretionary authority to vote on that proposal)
count as shares present for establishing a quorum.

The votes required for each proposal are as follows:
 

 

•  Required vote to approve the merger proposal: Approval of the merger proposal requires the affirmative vote of the holders
of a majority of the outstanding shares of DTS common stock entitled to vote in person or by proxy at the special meeting.
Accordingly, a DTS stockholder’s failure to vote, vote to abstain, or failure to instruct his or her broker or nominee to vote
will have the same effect as a vote “AGAINST” the merger proposal.

 

 

•  Required vote to approve the merger-related compensation proposal: Approval of the non-binding, advisory merger-related
compensation proposal requires the affirmative vote of the holders of a majority of the total number of votes of DTS
common stock represented at the special meeting and entitled to vote on such proposal. Accordingly, a DTS stockholder’s
failure to vote or failure to instruct his or her broker or nominee to vote will have no effect on the merger-related
compensation proposal; however, a DTS stockholder’s vote to abstain will have the same effect as a vote “AGAINST” the
merger-related compensation proposal.

 

 

•  Required vote to approve the adjournment proposal: Approval of the adjournment proposal requires the affirmative vote of
the holders of a majority of the total number of votes of DTS common stock represented at the special meeting and entitled
to vote on such proposal. Accordingly, a DTS stockholder’s failure to vote or failure to instruct his or her broker or nominee
to vote will have no effect on the adjournment proposal, assuming a quorum is present; however, a DTS stockholder’s vote
to abstain will have the same effect as a vote “AGAINST” the adjournment proposal.

Voting of Proxies

All shares represented by properly appointed proxies received in time for the special meeting will be voted at the special meeting
in the manner specified by the holders. Proxies that are properly appointed without voting instructions will be voted “FOR” the merger
proposal, “FOR” the merger-related compensation proposal and “FOR” the adjournment proposal.

To vote, please complete, sign, date and return the enclosed proxy card or, to appoint a proxy over the Internet or by telephone,
follow the instructions provided below. If you attend the special meeting and wish to vote in person, you may revoke your proxy
appointment and vote in person. If your shares are held in the name of your broker, bank or other nominee, you must obtain a proxy
appointment from the holder of record to be able to vote at the special meeting.

Voting over the Internet or by Telephone

You may also appoint a proxy to vote your shares over the Internet or by telephone. DTS’s Amended and Restated Bylaws (the
“bylaws”) and the Delaware General Corporation Law (the “DGCL”) specifically permit electronically appointed proxies, provided
that each such proxy appointment contains or is submitted with information from which the inspector of election can reasonably
assume that such proxy appointment was made or authorized by the stockholder.

The Internet and telephone voting procedures described below are designed to authenticate stockholders’ identities, to allow
stockholders to appoint a proxy to vote their shares and to confirm that stockholders’ instructions have been recorded properly.
Stockholders appointing a proxy to vote over the Internet should understand that there may be costs associated with electronic access,
such as usage charges from Internet access providers and telephone companies that must be borne by the stockholder.

For Shares of DTS Common Stock Registered in Your Name

Stockholders of record may go to www.investorvote.com/DTSI to appoint a proxy to vote their shares over the Internet. Have
your proxy card in hand when you access the web site and follow the instructions to obtain your records and to create an electronic
voting instruction form. Any stockholder may also appoint a proxy to vote shares by calling (800) 652-VOTE (8683) and following the
recorded instructions.

For Shares Registered in the Name of a Broker or a Bank

Most beneficial owners whose stock is held in street name receive instructions for authorizing votes by their banks, brokers or
other agents, rather than from our proxy card.

A number of brokers and banks are participating in a program that offers the means to authorize votes over the Internet and by
telephone. If your shares are held in an account with a broker or bank participating in such a program, you may appoint a proxy to vote
those shares over the Internet at the Internet URL specified on the instruction form received from your broker or bank, or by telephone
by calling the telephone number shown on the instruction form received from your broker or bank.

Revocability of Proxies

The appointment of a proxy on the enclosed proxy card or over the Internet or by telephone does not preclude a stockholder from
voting in person at the special meeting. You may revoke your proxy appointment at any time before the shares reflected on your proxy
card are voted at the special meeting in any one of the following ways:
 

 •  You may submit another properly completed proxy card with a later date.
 

 •  You may appoint a subsequent proxy by telephone or through the Internet.
 

 
•  You may send a timely written notice that you are revoking your proxy appointment to the Corporate Secretary of DTS, Inc.

at 5220 Las Virgenes Road, Calabasas, California 91302.
 

 
•  You may attend the special meeting and vote in person. However, simply attending the special meeting will not, by itself,

revoke your proxy appointment.

Your most current proxy card or telephone or Internet proxy appointment is the one that is counted. Please note that to be
effective, your new proxy card, Internet or telephonic voting instructions or written notice of revocation must be received by the
Corporate Secretary prior to the special meeting and, in the case of Internet or telephonic voting instructions, must be received by 11:59
p.m., Eastern time, on November 30, 2016.

Your attendance at the special meeting will not in and of itself constitute the revocation of a proxy appointment. If you have
instructed your broker to vote your shares, you must follow the directions received from your broker to change these instructions.

common share certificates will be mailed to our stockholders as soon as practicable after completion of the DTS merger.

Vote Required and DTS Board Recommendation

Under applicable law, we cannot complete the DTS merger without the affirmative vote of the holders of a majority of the

proposal. If you abstain from voting, fail to cast your vote, in person or by proxy, or fail to give voting instructions to your brokerage
firm, bank, trust or other nominee, it will have the same effect as a vote “AGAINST” the merger proposal.

At a duly convened meeting held on September 19, 2016, the DTS Board unanimously (i) approved the merger agreement and
consummation of the DTS merger upon the terms and subject to the conditions set forth in the merger agreement, (ii) determined that
the terms of the merger agreement and the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, including the DTS merger, are fair to,
advisable and in the best interests of DTS and its stockholders, (iii) directed that the merger agreement be submitted to DTS

the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, including the DTS merger. Accordingly, the DTS Board unanimously
recommends that DTS stockholders vote “FOR” the merger proposal.
