MERGER-RELATED COMPENSATION PROPOSAL

Golden Parachute Compensation

This section sets forth the information required by Item 402(t) of Regulation S-K regarding the compensation for each named
executive officer of DTS that is based on or otherwise relates to the DTS merger. This compensation is referred to as “golden
parachute” compensation by the applicable SEC disclosure rules, and in this section, we use such term to describe the merger-related
compensation payable, or that may become payable, to our named executive officers in connection with the DTS merger. The “golden
parachute” compensation payable, or that may become payable, to these individuals is subject to a non-binding, advisory vote of the
stockholders. For a summary of the terms and conditions of the payments and benefits described below, see the section of this proxy
statement entitled “The DTS Merger—Interests of DTS’s Directors and Executive Officers in the DTS Merger.”

Assuming that the DTS merger was completed on October 20, 2016 (the latest practicable date prior to filing this proxy
statement) and the employment of each of the named executive officers was terminated either by DTS without cause or by the named
executive officer for good reason immediately thereafter, each named executive officer would receive approximately the amounts set
forth in the table below, based on a $42.50 share price for each share of DTS common stock (the fixed dollar amount of the per share
merger consideration). As the table below assumes a qualifying termination of employment occurs immediately following the effective
time of the DTS merger, the amounts included below do not reflect any amounts which may be earned pursuant to the Retention Plan.

including the named executive officers, who continue as employees of Tessera, DTS, Holdco or one of their subsidiaries following the
effective time of the DTS merger, as discussed in the section of this proxy statement entitled “The DTS Merger—Interests of DTS’s

options and the vesting and settlement of DTS RSUs after the assumed completion date of the DTS merger). As a result, the actual
amounts, if any, to be received by a named executive officer may materially differ from the amounts set forth below.

Merger-Related Compensation

Section 14A of the Exchange Act, which was enacted as part of the Dodd-Frank Wall Street Reform and Consumer Protection
Act of 2010, requires that DTS provide DTS stockholders with the opportunity to vote to approve, on a non-binding, advisory basis, the
payment of certain compensation that will or may become payable by DTS to its named executive officers in connection with the DTS
merger.

DTS is asking DTS stockholders to indicate their approval of the compensation that will or may become payable by DTS to its
named executive officers in connection with the DTS merger as disclosed above in this section. In general, the various plans and
arrangements pursuant to which these compensation payments may be made formed part of DTS’s overall compensation program for
its named executive officers, and have previously been disclosed to DTS stockholders as part of the compensation discussion and
analysis and related sections of our annual proxy statements. The compensation committee of the DTS Board, which is composed
solely of non-employee directors, believes such compensatory arrangements to be reasonable.

The DTS Board encourages you to review carefully the named executive officer merger-related compensation information
disclosed in this proxy statement. The DTS Board unanimously recommends that DTS stockholders vote “FOR” the following
resolution:

“RESOLVED, that the compensation that may be paid or become payable to the named executive officers of DTS in connection
with the DTS merger, as disclosed pursuant to Item 402(t) of Regulation S-K in the golden parachute compensation table and
accompanying footnotes and narrative discussion set forth in this proxy statement under ‘Merger-Related Compensation Proposal—
Golden Parachute Compensation’ beginning on page 27, is hereby APPROVED.”

DTS stockholders should note that this proposal is not a condition to completion of the DTS merger, and as an advisory vote, the
result will not be binding on DTS or the DTS Board. Further, the underlying plans and arrangements are contractual in nature and not,
by their terms, subject to stockholder approval. Accordingly,

ADJOURNMENT PROPOSAL

If there are not sufficient votes at the time of the special meeting to approve the merger proposal, we intend to adjourn the special
meeting, if necessary or appropriate, to solicit additional proxies to vote in favor of the merger proposal. If stockholders approve the
adjournment proposal, we could adjourn the special meeting and any adjourned session of the special meeting and use the additional
time to solicit additional proxies, including proxies from stockholders that have previously returned properly executed proxies voting
against the merger proposal. Among other things, approval of the adjournment proposal could mean that, even if we had received
proxies representing a sufficient number of votes against the merger proposal such that the merger proposal would be defeated, we
could adjourn the special meeting without a vote on the merger proposal and seek to convince the holders of those shares to change
their votes to votes in favor of the merger proposal. Additionally, we may seek to adjourn the special meeting if a quorum is not present
or otherwise at the discretion of the chairman of the special meeting.

Vote Required and DTS Board Recommendation

Approval of the adjournment proposal requires the affirmative vote of the holders of a majority of the total number of votes of
DTS common stock represented at the special meeting and entitled to vote on such proposal. Accordingly, a DTS stockholder’s failure
to vote or failure to instruct his or her broker or nominee to vote will have no effect on the adjournment proposal, assuming a quorum is
present; however, a DTS stockholder’s vote to abstain will have the same effect as a vote “AGAINST” the adjournment proposal.
Accordingly, the DTS Board unanimously recommends that DTS stockholders vote “FOR” the adjournment proposal.

THE DTS MERGER

The discussion of the DTS merger contained in this section summarizes the material terms of the DTS merger. This summary may
not contain all of the information that is important to you. We urge you to read this proxy statement, the merger agreement, a copy of
which is attached to this proxy statement as Annex A, and the other documents referred to herein and therein (including the annexes)
carefully for a more complete understanding of the DTS merger.

Background of the DTS Merger

As part of its ongoing evaluation of DTS’s business, the DTS Board, together with senior management, regularly reviews and
assesses DTS’s operations and financial performance, industry conditions and regulatory developments that may impact DTS’s long-
term strategic goals and plans, including the review of potential opportunities for business combinations, acquisitions and other
financial and strategic alternatives as a means to enhance stockholder value. Over the last several years, the DTS Board has worked
with DTS’s financial advisor, Centerview, to assess potential strategic alternatives available to DTS, including at times contemplating a
potential sale of DTS, to enhance value to DTS’s stockholders.

In June 2014, Party A approached representatives of DTS expressing interest in a potential acquisition of DTS. Jon E. Kirchner,
DTS’s Chairman and Chief Executive Officer, met with representatives of Party A to discuss Party A’s strategic rationale and interest in
potentially acquiring DTS. Following such meeting, later in June 2014, representatives of DTS and representatives of Party A
negotiated and entered into a nondisclosure and standstill agreement pursuant to which DTS provided Party A with certain due
diligence information. In July 2014, members of DTS management and representatives of Centerview attended a series of diligence
meetings with representatives of Party A. In August 2014, Party A sent DTS a letter setting forth a non-binding indication of interest to
acquire all the of the common stock of DTS at a price ranging from $29.00 to $32.00 per share subject to continuing due diligence. Mr.
Kirchner promptly communicated the offer to the DTS Board. The DTS Board met to discuss the indication of interest, with
representatives of Centerview and DTS’s corporate counsel, DLA Piper LLP (US) (“DLA”) in attendance. DLA was generally invited
to attend all DTS Board and DTS Board committee meetings. After a representative from DLA described the DTS Board’s fiduciary
duties in connection with evaluating Party A’s proposal, the DTS Board discussed the proposal with members of management and
representatives of Centerview. After discussion of DTS’s prospects and long-term business plan and strategy, the DTS Board
determined that the execution of DTS’s current business strategy would deliver greater value to DTS’s stockholders than Party A’s
proposal. On that basis, the DTS Board instructed management of DTS to reject the proposal and ask Party A for a higher price. At the
instruction of the DTS Board, Mr. Kirchner informed representatives of Party A that DTS would not proceed with further diligence
efforts unless Party A’s offer improved.

In September and October 2014, Mr. Kirchner periodically met or spoke on the phone with representatives of Party A and Party A
continued to express an interest in a variety of strategic transactions with DTS, including a potential acquisition of DTS. In October
2014, Mr. Kirchner met informally with representatives of Party A who indicated an offer to acquire DTS may be forthcoming but
discussed internal challenges facing Party A regarding moving forward with a potential acquisition. Mr. Kirchner informed Party A
that the DTS Board would review any formal offer presented.

In late summer 2014 through early 2015, in response to Party A’s continued indications of interest in a potential acquisition of
DTS, Centerview, at the instruction of the DTS Board, contacted seven third parties regarding a potential strategic acquisition of DTS.
Each party subsequently responded to Centerview that such party was not interested in, or unable to pursue an acquisition of, DTS at
such time.

In January 2015, Mr. Kirchner met again informally with representatives of Party A. They discussed, among other things, updates
in their respective businesses and continued mutual interest in a potential strategic transaction. Representatives of Party A expressed an
interest in potentially pursuing an acquisition following the reporting of its fiscal year end results.
 

32



8/19/2019 DEFM14A

https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1226308/000119312516744017/d215313ddefm14a.htm 42/256

Table of Contents

In March 2015, Mr. Kirchner met with representatives of Party A and Party A reiterated its interest in a potential acquisition of
DTS but expressed concern over the increase in DTS’s valuation and the then current valuation of Party A’s equity, and indicated that it
would be unable to pursue an acquisition at the current time.

In April 2015, representatives of Centerview contacted Party B to discuss a potential business combination with DTS.
Representatives of each of DTS, Centerview and Party B met to provide an overview of their respective businesses and discuss the
merits of a potential business combination. Following the meeting, Party B and DTS entered into a nondisclosure and standstill
agreement and DTS provided certain due diligence materials to Party B. During May through July 2015, Party B performed diligence
and had a series of calls and meetings with representatives of DTS to discuss diligence issues and Party B’s interest in a potential
acquisition of DTS.

On July 31, 2015, representatives of Party B contacted Mr. Kirchner to express interest in certain aspects of DTS and indicated
the Party B’s financial advisors were in the process of preparing an indication of interest. Mr. Kirchner informed Party B that the DTS
Board would consider any formal offer presented. In early August 2015, representatives of Party B, including Party B’s financial
advisors, contacted representatives of DTS, including Centerview, indicating a desire to acquire DTS for $35.00 per share, but
requested a 90-day exclusivity period and conditioned the indication of interest on the completion of several ongoing strategic matters
in which Party B was involved. Mr. Kirchner instructed Centerview to request additional information regarding the potential offer and
the various associated contingencies, but calls placed by representatives of Centerview to representatives of Party B were not returned.

On August 5, 2015, Mr. Kirchner exchanged emails with representatives of Party B indicating that DTS could not proceed with
any exclusivity period without having more certainty around the various conditions and contingencies outlined in previous discussions.
Party B indicated that it was not in a position to provide such certainty until after it settled its ongoing strategic matters. As such, DTS
concluded Party B was not prepared to proceed with an acquisition on terms, including with respect to exclusivity and conditionality,
that would have been acceptable to DTS.

In August 2015, Tom Lacey, Chief Executive Officer of Tessera, contacted Mr. Kirchner requesting a meeting to discuss certain
issues impacting technology licensing companies.

In October 2015, Party B contacted Mr. Kirchner to congratulate him on DTS’s recent acquisition of iBiquity Digital Corporation.
Party B also expressed that it was unable to pursue an acquisition at that time but was potentially interested in exploring a commercial
transaction with DTS.

On November 5, 2015, Mr. Lacey and Mr. Kirchner met in person in Southern California and discussed issues, challenges and
opportunities in the technology industry with a specific focus on trends impacting licensing companies within the industry.

On January 7, 2016, Mr. Lacey and Mr. Kirchner met in Las Vegas at the Consumer Electronics Show and Mr. Lacey expressed
interest in a potential business combination transaction between DTS and Tessera. Messrs. Lacey and Kirchner agreed to have a further
discussion about the potential merits of such a transaction. DTS and Tessera subsequently entered into a nondisclosure and standstill
agreement dated January 12, 2016.

On January 22, 2016, Mr. Lacey received a telephone call from Mr. Kirchner to discuss a planned upcoming meeting between the
companies’ respective senior management and financial advisors. Mr. Kirchner indicated to Mr. Lacey that while the DTS Board was
receptive to discussing an acquisition proposal from Tessera, DTS would need to analyze the strategic rationale for a sale as compared
to its standalone plan. Mr. Kirchner also indicated that DTS would expect any exclusivity period to be short.

On January 25, 2016, senior management from DTS met with senior management from Tessera to present an overview of their
respective companies and to preliminarily discuss the merits of a potential business combination.
 

33



8/19/2019 DEFM14A

https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1226308/000119312516744017/d215313ddefm14a.htm 43/256

Table of Contents

On February 3, 2016, Mr. Kirchner received a telephone call from Mr. Lacey to discuss the January 25, 2016 meeting and provide
additional information as to the merits of a potential business combination between DTS and Tessera.

On February 5, 2016, senior management of Tessera and DTS and representatives of Centerview and Tessera’s financial advisor,
GCA Advisors, LLC (“GCA”), held a telephone call to outline the possible steps that would be involved in an acquisition of DTS.
Centerview indicated they had received an initial diligence request list from GCA and had begun to review it. DTS senior management
noted that they remained busy with the integration of the iBiquity acquisition. The parties agreed that the next step would be to have a
management meeting, including representatives of Centerview and GCA, to more fully discuss the strategic vision of both companies
and sources of potential synergies.

On February 17, 2016, senior management from DTS, together with representatives of Centerview, held a telephone call with
senior management from Tessera, together with representatives of GCA, to discuss DTS’s licensing business.

On February 19, 2016, senior management from DTS, together with representatives of Centerview, met with senior management
from Tessera, together with representatives of GCA, to provide a more comprehensive overview of the respective companies, including
current strategy and operations. At such meeting, DTS agreed to make certain additional diligence materials available to Tessera
through an online data room.

On March 15, 2016, Mr. Kirchner and Mr. Lacey discussed broadly the terms of a potential transaction but agreed to postpone
further discussions until after the announcement of DTS’s first quarter 2016 earnings.

On April 12, 2016, Mr. Kirchner met Mr. Lacey at Tessera’s offices for an office tour and discussed broadly DTS’s organizational
structure and key business drivers.

On May 18, 2016, Mr. Kirchner and Mr. Lacey met informally and discussed, among other things, business updates relating to
their respective organizations. Mr. Lacey reiterated Tessera’s interest in an acquisition.

On May 19, 2016, Mr. Lacey called Mr. Kirchner to discuss Tessera’s interest in moving forward with an offer to acquire DTS.
Mr. Kirchner informed Mr. Lacey that the DTS Board would review and evaluate any formal offer presented. Following the call,
Tessera sent DTS a letter setting forth a non-binding indication of interest to acquire all the common stock of DTS at a price of $31.50
per share. The indication of interest stated that the offer could consist of a meaningful amount of Tessera equity, at the election of DTS
stockholders. Mr. Kirchner promptly informed the DTS Board of the indication of interest.

On May 20, 2016, Mr. Kirchner called Mr. Lacey to inform him that the DTS Board would meet on May 22, 2016 to consider
Tessera’s offer, but that based on DTS’s standalone plan and prior guidance from the DTS Board, Tessera’s offer was likely to be
inadequate.

DTS common stock closed at $23.56 per share on May 20, 2016, and on May 22, 2016, prior to the market having reopened, the
DTS Board held a telephonic meeting to discuss Tessera’s May 19, 2016 proposal. After a representative from DLA described the DTS
Board’s fiduciary duties in connection with evaluating Tessera’s May 19, 2016 proposal, the DTS Board discussed the proposal in
detail. After discussion of DTS’s prospects as a standalone company as compared to Tessera’s offer of $31.50 per share, the DTS Board
determined that its preliminary view was that the execution of DTS’s current business strategy would deliver greater value to DTS’s
stockholders than Tessera’s May 19, 2016 proposal and the DTS Board concluded that it was not in the best interests of stockholders to
pursue a sale at that time. Following discussions, the DTS Board authorized management to communicate to Tessera that it appreciated
Tessera’s continued interest in DTS, but that DTS was not prepared to sell at that time.

On May 24, 2016, Mr. Kirchner informed Mr. Lacey that the DTS Board had concluded that the May 19, 2016 proposal
undervalued DTS and its future prospects and that the DTS Board was committed to executing DTS’s current standalone business
strategy. DTS did not make a specific counteroffer at this time.

After market close on August 8, 2016, DTS reported its preliminary financial results for the second quarter of 2016, which
exceeded DTS’s guidance and analyst expectations, raised the lower end of its 2016 annual revenue guidance and provided forecasted
revenue projections for 2020, including revenue forecasts for each of its home, automotive and mobile businesses. The closing price of
DTS’s common stock on August 8, 2016, was $29.21, and on August 9, 2016, the first trading day after that announcement, the closing
price of DTS’s common stock was $33.02.

On August 9, 2016, representatives of GCA contacted representatives of Centerview to determine if DTS was still interested in
discussing a potential business combination. Subsequently, Mr. Lacey contacted Mr. Kirchner and requested that Mr. Kirchner and
representatives of DTS meet with representatives of Tessera and provide an update on DTS’s business. Mr. Lacey expressed an interest
in resuming discussions about a potential business combination and indicated that subject to due diligence and approval by the Tessera
Board, Tessera could potentially revise its indication of interest upward to $40.00 per share.

On August 10, 2016, GCA sent Centerview a financial due diligence request list.

On August 11, 2016, Mr. Lacey called Mr. Kirchner to discuss the due diligence information Tessera would need in order to raise
its offer to $40.00 per share.

On August 12, 2016, at Tessera’s request, Mr. Kirchner and representatives of DTS, along with representatives of Centerview, met
with representatives of Tessera, including Mr. Lacey and representatives of GCA to provide a presentation of DTS’s business and
answer diligence questions. Tessera and GCA were subsequently provided access to a virtual data room containing certain business and
financial data. Having received the necessary diligence information and being satisfied with DTS’s responses, Mr. Lacey raised
Tessera’s offer to $40.00 per share. Based upon previous guidance from the DTS Board and management and Centerview’s preliminary
analysis of DTS’s standalone plan, Mr. Kirchner indicated that he believed the DTS Board would be receptive to an offer of $45.00 per
share in cash.

On August 17, 2016, the DTS Board held a meeting at DTS’s offices, with a representative from DLA in attendance.

On August 17, 2016, during a regularly scheduled DTS Board meeting, Mr. Kirchner received from Mr. Lacey an unsolicited,
verbal proposal to purchase all of DTS’s outstanding shares of common stock, in an all cash transaction, at a price per share of $42.00,
or approximately a 28% premium to the closing price of DTS’s common stock on the prior day and approximately a 27% premium to
the then 52-week high closing price of DTS’s common stock. Mr. Kirchner promptly presented the offer to the DTS Board. After a
representative from DLA described the DTS Board’s fiduciary duties in connection with evaluating Tessera’s August 17, 2016
proposal, the DTS Board discussed the proposal. At that meeting, the DTS Board instructed DTS’s senior management to work with
Centerview to evaluate the offer and prepare a preliminary presentation for the continuation of the DTS Board meeting scheduled for
the next day.

Following the DTS Board meeting on August 17, 2016, representatives of Centerview, at the request and direction of the DTS
Board, conducted a targeted outreach to certain third parties including third parties who had previously indicated an interest in
exploring a potential strategic transaction with DTS, as well as one additional third party, to determine other potential strategic
alternatives. On August 17, 2016, a representative of Centerview contacted a representative of Party A to gauge interest in a possible
strategic transaction. Party A responded on August 18, 2016, that it would review the potential opportunity internally. Later that week,
Party A contacted Centerview and indicated that it was unable to pursue an acquisition at this time.

On August 18, 2016, representatives of Centerview presented to the DTS Board the results of Centerview’s preliminary analysis
of Tessera’s proposed offer, which analysis included a financial analysis of DTS’s historical and potential future operating performance
and plans, as prepared by management and reviewed by the DTS Board, industry conditions and various potential strategic alternatives
and opportunities. After discussion of DTS’s prospects as a standalone business and the proposal from Tessera with representatives of
Centerview, the DTS Board asked management to work with Centerview to determine whether Tessera would increase its offer.
Following the meeting, Mr. Kirchner contacted Mr. Lacey and told him that while the DTS Board was appreciative of Tessera’s
interest, it would like to see Tessera improve its offer. At the instruction of the DTS Board, Mr. Kirchner countered at $43.00 per share.

Also on August 18, 2016, a representative of Centerview spoke with representatives of Party B to gauge interest in a potential
acquisition of DTS. Later that week, Party B contacted Centerview and indicated that it was unable to pursue an acquisition at this
time. Representatives of Centerview also spoke with representatives of GCA regarding financial modeling, Tessera’s request for
exclusivity and a prospective definitive agreement.

On August 19, 2016, Mr. Lacey contacted Mr. Kirchner to present an improved, verbal proposal to purchase all of DTS’s
outstanding shares of common stock, in an all cash transaction, at a price per share of $42.50, indicating that this price represented
Tessera’s best and final offer. DTS’s closing stock price on August 18, 2016, the trading day immediately prior to the offer, was $33.18.
In addition, representatives of GCA, indicated to representatives of Centerview that Tessera would require 30 days of exclusivity as
part of its offer. Representatives of DTS, including representatives of Centerview, indicated that DTS would need to conduct additional
market analysis and require an opportunity to investigate alternative proposals prior to consummating a transaction with Tessera.
Representatives of GCA indicated that Tessera would not proceed with the transaction unless Tessera was granted exclusivity. Mr.
Kirchner promptly communicated the offer to the DTS Board. After discussion, the DTS Board instructed senior management to
continue discussions with Tessera regarding a potential transaction and to provide additional due diligence information to Tessera and
to negotiate the terms of an exclusivity agreement with Tessera, provided that senior management, together with representatives of
Centerview, first have an opportunity to investigate alternative proposals.

On August 19, 2016, DLA sent an initial draft of the merger agreement to Skadden, Arps, Slate, Meagher & Flom LLP
(“Skadden”), Tessera’s legal counsel. Later that evening, Skadden contacted DLA to provide Tessera’s initial high-level comments to
the draft merger agreement.

On August 20, 2016, representatives of DTS, Centerview and DLA discussed Tessera’s initial high-level comments to the draft
merger agreement. Also on August 20, 2016, Skadden provided to DLA an initial draft exclusivity agreement.

On August 21, 2016, DLA contacted Skadden to provide DTS’s initial comments to the exclusivity agreement, indicating that
DTS would not agree to any exclusivity arrangement prior to being able to conduct additional market analysis and an opportunity to
investigate alternative proposals. Following this discussion, Mr. Kirchner contacted Mr. Lacey to discuss DTS’s need to conduct
additional market analysis and an opportunity to investigate alternative proposals. Representatives of Centerview and representatives of
GCA had conversations on the same matter.

From August 21 to August 24, Mr. Kirchner and Mr. Lacey discussed by telephone on several occasions the terms of an
exclusivity agreement. In addition, DLA and Skadden had discussions regarding the terms of an exclusivity agreement to begin no
earlier than August 29, 2016, exchanging several drafts.

On August 22, 2016, senior management from DTS provided Tessera’s senior management with an overview of DTS’s financial
projections.

During the period between August 22 and August 28, 2016, representatives of Centerview contacted several representatives of
eight potential strategic bidders, including representatives of Parties A and B, as well as five of

the seven parties contacted during late summer 2014 through early 2015. All contacted potential strategic bidders either did not

On August 25, 2016, Mr. Lacey and Mr. Kirchner, along with Tessera’s Chief Financial Officer, Robert Andersen, met in San
Francisco to discuss organizational and potential cost synergies that could result from the business combination.

On August 26, 2016, members of Tessera’s senior management met with DTS’s Chief Financial Officer, Mel Flanigan to discuss

On August 29, 2016, the DTS Board held a telephonic meeting, at which representatives of DTS’s senior management,
Centerview and DLA were present, to discuss the status of Tessera’s August 19, 2016 proposal. After a representative of DLA
counseled the DTS Board with respect to their fiduciary duties, representatives of Centerview provided an overview of the status of

continue discussions with Tessera under the exclusivity agreement as negotiated by DLA.

Also on August 29, 2016 Messrs. Lacey, Kirchner and Andersen discussed certain general employee matters in connection with
the transaction.

On August 30, 2016, DTS entered into exclusivity with Tessera on the terms negotiated by DLA.

From August 30, 2016 until the execution of the definitive merger agreement on September 19, 2016, the companies and their
respective advisors exchanged numerous drafts of the merger agreement and engaged in negotiations and discussions regarding the
terms and conditions of the merger agreement. Significant areas of negotiation included the scope of representations and warranties and
interim operating covenants, the conditions to closing, the structure of the transaction, the terms upon which DTS could consider an
alternative acquisition proposal and the process for dealing with any such proposal and the amount and triggers for the possible
reimbursement of expenses and the payment of termination fees. The parties discussed extensively whether DTS would be permitted to
terminate the merger agreement to accept a superior proposal or would be required to submit the merger agreement to a vote of its
stockholders, even if it received such a proposal. The parties also discussed various employee benefit and other employee- and
compensation-related provisions of the merger agreement, including senior management compensation issues.

Concurrent with these discussions, representatives of management of each of the companies, Skadden, DLA and the companies’
respective other representatives continued to have numerous discussions by teleconference to review and discuss, among other things,
due diligence, a retention plan for DTS employees, Tessera’s proposed financing for the potential transaction, the terms of the merger
agreement and the timeline for the potential transaction.

On August 31, 2016, DTS made available to Tessera and its representatives an online data room containing certain additional
information concerning DTS, supplementing the information provided on August 12, 2016. During the period beginning on August 31,
2016 and extending through the date of the execution of the merger agreement, the parties conducted due diligence investigations with
respect to DTS’s business, legal, regulatory, technology and other matters, including financial forecasts, and held discussions
concerning their respective businesses and prospects and the potential synergies and commercial benefits that could result from the
potential transaction.

On September 6, 2016, representatives of DTS, DLA, Tessera and Skadden held a telephonic meeting to discuss diligence
matters.

On September 7, 2016, Skadden provided comprehensive comments to the draft merger agreement to DLA. From September 7 to
September 11, 2016, DTS and DLA reviewed and revised the draft merger agreement.

On September 11, 2016, the DTS Board held a telephonic conference with representatives of senior management and DLA to
review the comments to the draft merger agreement and discuss a number of open matters, including, among other things, deal
structure, the circumstances under which the agreement could be terminated, the circumstances under which a termination fee would be
payable, the DTS Board’s fiduciary obligations, the scope of the representations, warranties and covenants included in the draft merger
agreement and the treatment of outstanding DTS equity awards. Following the meeting, DLA provided to Skadden DTS’s comments to
the draft merger agreement.

From September 12 through September 14, 2016, representatives of DLA and Skadden held a series of conference calls to
negotiate the terms of the merger agreement.

On September 13, 2016, senior management of Tessera and DTS met in San Jose, California to discuss technology related due
diligence questions and potential synergies, and representatives of Tessera and DTS met in Calabasas to discuss tax-related due
diligence.

On September 14, 2016, senior management of Tessera and DTS, including Mr. Lacey and Mr. Kirchner, met in Calabasas to
discuss business due diligence.

On September 14 and September 15, 2016, Mr. Kirchner and Mr. Lacey held multiple calls to discuss certain outstanding issues
relating to the transaction, including the status of diligence, process for communication of the transaction if executed, and the potential
timing for completing the negotiation of the merger agreement.

From September 16, 2016, through September 18, 2016, Tessera, DTS and their respective representatives continued to negotiate
the terms of a definitive merger agreement and conducted numerous due diligence conference calls regarding DTS’s business.

On September 17, 2016, senior management of DTS and Tessera and their investor relations advisors reviewed and discussed
prospective merger announcement communications materials in the event Tessera and DTS entered into a definitive acquisition
agreement.

On September 18, 2016, the DTS Board met telephonically to discuss the status of the proposed transaction with Tessera.
Together with management and DTS’s external financial and legal advisors, the DTS Board reviewed the developments that had taken
place since the last DTS Board meeting, including the progress that had been made in negotiations with Tessera. Representatives of
DLA described the material terms of the proposed transaction and the merger agreement, a current draft of which had been circulated
in advance of the meeting, and the status of the issues remaining to be agreed upon, which the DTS Board discussed in detail.
Representatives of Centerview, reviewing materials prepared and distributed to the DTS Board in advance of the meeting, discussed its
preliminary financial analysis of the merger consideration, and a preliminary analysis of the premium represented by the merger
consideration. The DTS Board, along with its legal and financial advisors, also reviewed and discussed (i) the various strategic
alternatives (including DTS’s standalone plan) that the DTS Board had considered up to that point, including the likelihood of any third
parties having an interest in offering, or being prepared to offer, a more attractive alternative to a transaction with Tessera, (ii) the
relative advantages and disadvantages of a transaction with Tessera in comparison to such strategic alternatives, (iii) the business and
strategic risks and opportunities associated with the various alternatives (including any regulatory risks associated therewith) and (iv)
DTS’s standalone plan. The DTS Board also discussed, together with representatives of Centerview and DLA, Tessera’s financing for
the proposed transaction, including the absence

of a financing condition to the consummation of the proposed transaction. In addition, representatives of DLA discussed with the DTS

On September 19, the DTS Board held a telephonic meeting to discuss the terms of the proposed transaction and the fully
negotiated merger agreement, a copy of which had been distributed in advance of the meeting, and the developments since the previous
meeting. Together with management and DTS’s external financial and legal advisors, the DTS Board reviewed the results of
Centerview’s financial analysis and the terms of the proposed transaction. Representatives of DLA updated the DTS Board on the
negotiations with Tessera since the previous DTS Board meeting and reviewed with the DTS Board the material terms of the merger
agreement. Representatives of Centerview reviewed with the DTS Board Centerview’s financial analysis of the merger consideration,
and rendered to the DTS Board an oral opinion, which was subsequently confirmed by delivery of a written opinion dated such date
that, as of such date and based upon and subject to various assumptions made, procedures followed, matters considered, and
qualifications and limitations upon the review undertaken in preparing its opinion, the merger consideration to be paid to the holders of
Shares (other than certain Shares excluded as specified in such opinion) pursuant to the merger agreement was fair, from a financial
point of view, to such holders. For a detailed discussion of Centerview’s opinion, please refer to the section entitled “The DTS Merger
—Opinion of Centerview Partners LLC” beginning on page 46. The DTS Board also considered the factors described below under
“The DTS Merger—Recommendation of the DTS Board; Reasons for the DTS Merger”, as well as regulatory approval risks, the
process of SEC review, the financing requirements of the proposed transaction and the various risks, such as non-consummation of the
mergers, arising in connection with the proposed transaction. Following extensive discussion of all of the foregoing by the DTS Board,
the DTS Board unanimously (i) approved the merger agreement and consummation of the DTS merger upon the terms and subject to
the conditions set forth in the merger agreement, (ii) determined that the terms of the merger agreement and the transactions
contemplated by the merger agreement, including the DTS merger, are fair to, advisable and in the best interests of DTS and its
stockholders, (iii) directed that the merger agreement be submitted to DTS stockholders for adoption at the special meeting and (iv)
recommend that DTS stockholders adopt the merger agreement and approve the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement,
including the DTS merger. The DTS Board then instructed senior management to finalize the transaction documents and enter into the
merger agreement consistent with its instructions.

On September 19, 2016, the last full trading day before the announcement of the merger agreement, the closing price of DTS
shares was $34.33.

After the execution of the debt commitment letter, a copy of which was provided to DTS and its financial and legal advisors, each
of Tessera, DTS, Holdco, Parent Merger Sub and Company Merger Sub executed and delivered the merger agreement, effective as of
September 19, 2016. On the morning of September 20, 2016, before trading began, Tessera and DTS issued a joint press release
announcing the transaction.

Recommendation of the DTS Board; Reasons for the DTS Merger

At a duly convened meeting held on September 19, 2016, the DTS Board unanimously (i) approved the merger agreement and
consummation of the DTS merger upon the terms and subject to the conditions set forth in the merger agreement, (ii) determined that
the terms of the merger agreement and the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, including the DTS merger, are fair to
advisable and in the best interests of DTS and its stockholders, (iii) directed that the merger agreement be submitted to DTS
stockholders for adoption at the special meeting and (iv) recommended that DTS stockholders adopt the merger agreement and approve
the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, including the DTS merger.

ACCORDINGLY, THE DTS BOARD UNANIMOUSLY RECOMMENDS THAT DTS STOCKHOLDERS VOTE “FOR”
THE MERGER PROPOSAL, “FOR” THE MERGER-RELATED COMPENSATION PROPOSAL AND “FOR” THE
ADJOURNMENT PROPOSAL.

In evaluating the merger agreement and the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, including the DTS merger, the
DTS Board consulted with DTS management, its financial advisor and outside legal counsel. In recommending that stockholders vote
in favor of adoption of the merger agreement, including the DTS merger, the DTS Board considered a number of positive factors,
including the following (which factors are not necessarily exhaustive or presented in order of relative importance):
 

 
•  the all-cash nature of the consideration that DTS stockholders will be entitled to receive in connection with the DTS merger,

which allows DTS stockholders to realize immediate value, in cash, for their investment in DTS, while enabling
stockholders to avoid further risk of investment in DTS;

 

 •  the relationship of the $42.50 per share consideration to the historical trading price of DTS common stock, including:
 

 
•  the fact that the per share merger consideration represents a premium of approximately 24% over the closing price of

DTS’s shares of $34.33 on September 19, 2016, or one day prior to the public announcement of the execution of the
merger agreement;

 

 
•  the fact that the per share merger consideration represents a premium of approximately 26% over the volume-

weighted average closing stock price of a share of DTS’s common stock during the thirty days ended September 19,
2016; and

 

 
•  the fact that the per share merger consideration represents a premium of approximately 24% over DTS’s 52-week

high for the period ended September 19, 2016;
 

 
•  the fact that DTS, together with management and its financial advisor, contacted several potential acquirors regarding a sale

of DTS;
 

 

•  the opinion of Centerview rendered to the DTS Board on September 19, 2016, which was subsequently confirmed by
delivery of a written opinion dated such date that, as of such date and based upon and subject to the assumptions made,
procedures followed, matters considered, and qualifications and limitations upon the review undertaken by Centerview in
preparing its opinion, the merger consideration to be paid to the holders of Shares (other than certain shares excluded as
specified in such opinion) pursuant to the merger agreement was fair, from a financial point of view, to such holders, as more
fully described in the section entitled “The DTS Merger—Opinion of Centerview Partners LLC;” beginning on page 46;

 

 •  the terms of the merger agreement, including:
 

 
•  the ability of the parties to consummate the DTS merger, including the fact that Tessera’s obligation to complete the

DTS merger is not conditioned upon receipt of financing and that Tessera has obtained from RBC a debt commitment
letter that is believed to be on customary and commercially reasonable terms;

 

 
•  DTS’s ability, under certain circumstances, to furnish information to and conduct negotiations with third parties

regarding alternative acquisition proposals;
 

 
•  DTS’s ability to terminate the merger agreement in order to accept a superior proposal, subject to the ability of

Tessera to match such superior proposal and subject to paying Tessera a termination fee of $25,500,000;
 

 
•  the fact that the DTS Board believed that the termination fee of  $25,500,000 is reasonable and not preclusive of other

offers;
 

 •  DTS’s entitlement to specific performance to prevent breaches of the merger agreement;
 

 
•  the fact that the merger agreement is subject to the approval of holders of a majority of the outstanding shares of DTS

common stock; and
 

 
•  the DTS Board’s view that the merger agreement was the product of arms’-length negotiation and contained

customary terms and conditions;

•  the DTS Board’s analysis of DTS’s background, recent operating history and current position in the marketplace in its

deliberations concerning the DTS merger and the other transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, including:
 

 
•  DTS’s business and industry, financial condition, historical and projected financial performance, competitive position

and assets and prospects, as well as current industry, economic and market conditions and trends in the markets DTS

•  the DTS Board’s consideration of DTS’s current operating plan, including the opportunities and risks facing DTS in

executing on such operating plan together with certain forecasts for DTS prepared by DTS management, and the
present value of DTS based on those projections, together with the risks associated with achieving such forecasts; and

 

 

•  the DTS Board’s consideration of the perceived risks and benefits of a variety of strategic alternatives for DTS,
including (1) the continuation of DTS’s business plan as an independent enterprise, (2) modifications to DTS’s
strategy and operating plan, (3) potential expansion opportunities into new business segments through acquisitions
and combinations of DTS with other businesses, (4) potential divestitures and (5) a possible sale of DTS;

 

 

•  the DTS Board’s consideration that DTS has explored various alternatives to an acquisition by Tessera, including those
described immediately above, and that such alternatives were not reasonably likely to create greater value for DTS’s
stockholders than the transaction with Tessera, taking into account execution risk as well as business, competitive, industry
and market risk;

 

 
•  the DTS Board’s belief that it had negotiated the highest price per share for DTS common stock that Tessera was willing to

pay, which negotiations are more fully described above in “The DTS Merger—Background of the DTS Merger”; and
 

 

•  the DTS Board’s view that the terms of the merger agreement would be unlikely to deter interested third parties from making
a superior proposal, including the merger agreement’s terms and conditions as they relate to the DTS Board’s ability to
change its recommendation with respect to the DTS merger and the belief that the termination fee potentially payable to
Tessera is reasonable in light of the circumstances, consistent with comparable transactions and not preclusive of other
offers.

The DTS Board also considered a number of uncertainties, risks and potentially negative factors in its deliberations concerning
the DTS merger, including the following (which factors are not necessarily exhaustive or presented in order of relative importance):
 

 
•  the risks and costs to DTS if the DTS merger does not close, including the potential effect on DTS’s business and

relationships with customers, as well as the potential effect of the resulting public announcement of the termination of the
merger agreement on the trading price of DTS common stock;

 

 

•  the fact that the announcement and pendency of the DTS merger, or the failure to complete the DTS merger, may cause
substantial harm to DTS’s relationships with its employees (including making it more difficult to attract and retain key
personnel and the possible loss of key management, technical, sales and other personnel), vendors and customers and may
divert employees’ attention away from DTS’s day-to-day business operations;

 

 
•  the fact that DTS’s stockholders will receive the per share merger consideration in cash and will no longer have the

opportunity to participate in any future earnings or growth of DTS or benefit from any potential future appreciation in the
value of DTS shares, including any value that could be achieved if DTS engages in future strategic or other transactions;

 

 
•  the fact that, subject to the terms and conditions of the merger agreement, DTS cannot solicit other acquisition proposals,

which could reduce the likelihood that other potential acquirers would propose an alternative transaction that may be more
advantageous to DTS’s stockholders, and must pay Tessera

a termination fee of $25,500,000 under certain circumstances following termination of the merger agreement, including if
the DTS Board desires to terminate the merger agreement to accept a superior proposal;

 

 

•  the restrictions on the conduct of DTS’s business prior to the consummation of the DTS merger, including the requirement
that DTS conduct its business in the ordinary course, subject to specific limitations, which may delay or prevent DTS from
undertaking business opportunities that may arise before the completion of the DTS merger and that, absent the merger
agreement, DTS might have pursued;

 

 
•  the fact that an all cash transaction would be taxable to DTS’s stockholders that are U.S. persons for U.S. federal income tax

purposes;
 

 
•  the significant costs involved in connection with entering into the merger agreement and completing the DTS merger and the

substantial time and effort of DTS management required to complete the DTS merger, which may disrupt DTS’s business
operations;

 

 
•  the fact that Tessera requires substantial third party debt financing for the transaction, and in the event that such third party

financing is not available to Tessera, Tessera may not have the financial resources to consummate the DTS Merger; and
 

 
•  the fact that DTS’s directors and officers may have interests in the DTS merger that may be different from, or in addition to,

those of DTS’s other stockholders (see “The DTS Merger—Interests of DTS’s Directors and Executive Officers in the DTS
Merger”).

The foregoing discussion of the information and factors considered by the DTS Board is not intended to be exhaustive, but
summarizes the material factors considered by the DTS Board in its consideration of the merger agreement and the transactions
contemplated thereby, including the DTS merger. In view of the variety of factors considered in connection with its evaluation of the
DTS merger, the DTS Board did not find it practicable to, and did not, quantify or otherwise assign relative weights to the specific
factors considered in reaching its determination and recommendation. In addition, individual directors may have given different
weights to different factors. The DTS Board did not undertake to make any specific determination as to whether any factor, or any
particular aspect of any factor, supported or did not support its ultimate determination. The DTS Board based its recommendation on
the totality of the information presented.

After considering these and other factors, the DTS Board concluded that the potential benefits of the DTS merger greatly
outweighed the risks, uncertainties, restrictions and potentially adverse factors. Accordingly, the DTS Board unanimously (i) approved
the merger agreement and consummation of the DTS merger upon the terms and subject to the conditions set forth in the merger
agreement, (ii) determined that the terms of the merger agreement and the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement,
including the DTS merger, are fair to, advisable and in the best interests of DTS and its stockholders, (iii) directed that the merger
agreement be submitted to DTS stockholders for adoption at the special meeting and (iv) recommended that DTS stockholders adopt
the merger agreement and approve the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement, including the DTS merger.

In considering the recommendation of the DTS Board, you should be aware that certain of DTS’s directors and executive officers
may have interests in the DTS merger that are different from, or in addition to, yours. The DTS Board was aware of and considered
these interests, among other matters, in evaluating the merger agreement and the transactions contemplated thereby, and in
recommending that the stockholders adopt the merger agreement and approve the transactions contemplated by the merger agreement,
including the DTS merger. See the section entitled “The DTS Merger—Interests of DTS’s Directors and Executive Officers in the DTS
Merger” beginning on page 53.

Certain Financial Forecasts

DTS Summary Unaudited Prospective Financial Information

DTS does not as a matter of course make public detailed long-term projections as to future revenues, earnings or other results due
to, among other reasons, the uncertainty of the underlying assumptions and estimates. However, in connection with the review of the
mergers, DTS management prepared unaudited prospective financial information for DTS on a standalone basis, without giving effect
to the mergers. DTS is electing to provide the summary unaudited prospective financial information in this section of the proxy
statement to provide the stockholders of DTS access to certain non-public unaudited prospective financial information that was made
available to DTS’s financial advisor in connection with rendering its fairness opinion. (See the section entitled “The DTS Merger—
Opinion of Centerview Partners LLC” beginning on page 46). The unaudited prospective financial information was not prepared with a
view toward public disclosure and the inclusion of summary unaudited prospective financial information below should not be regarded
as an indication that any of DTS, Tessera or any other recipient of this information considered, or now considers, it to be necessarily
predictive of actual future results. DTS does not assume any responsibility to stockholders for the accuracy of this information.

Although the unaudited prospective financial information was, in general, prepared for internal use by DTS and its financial
advisor and is subjective in many respects and thus subject to interpretation, it was also made available to the DTS Board, Tessera and
Tessera’s financial advisor, GCA. While presented with numeric specificity, the unaudited prospective financial information reflects
numerous estimates and assumptions made by the management of DTS with respect to industry performance and competition, general
business, economic, market and financial conditions and matters specific to DTS’s business, all of which are difficult to predict and
many of which are beyond DTS’s control. As a result, there can be no assurance that the unaudited prospective financial information
will be realized or that actual results will not be significantly higher or lower than estimated. Since the unaudited prospective financial
information covers multiple years, such information by its nature becomes less predictive with each successive year. Stockholders are
urged to review DTS’s most recent SEC filings for a description of risk factors with respect to DTS’s business. See also “Special Note
Regarding Forward-Looking Statements” beginning on page 19 and “Where You Can Find More Information” beginning on page 96.
The unaudited prospective financial information was not prepared with a view toward complying with U.S. GAAP, the published
guidelines of the SEC regarding projections or the guidelines established by the American Institute of Certified Public Accountants for
preparation and presentation of prospective financial information.

The unaudited prospective financial information included in this section of the proxy statement has been prepared by, and is the
responsibility of, DTS’s management. Deloitte & Touche LLP has neither examined, compiled nor performed any procedures with
respect to the accompanying prospective financial information and, accordingly, Deloitte & Touche LLP does not express an opinion or
any other form of assurance with respect thereto. The Deloitte & Touche LLP reports incorporated by reference in this proxy statement
relate to DTS’s historical financial information only. They do not extend to the unaudited prospective financial information and should
not be read to do so.

The DTS management forecasts were prepared based on DTS as a standalone company. Such forecasts do not take into account
the mergers, including the impact of negotiating or executing the transaction, the expenses that may be incurred in connection with
consummating the mergers, the potential synergies that may be achieved by the combined company as a result of the mergers, the
effect of any business or strategic decision or action that has been or will be taken as a result of the merger agreement having been
executed, or the effect of any business or strategic decisions or actions which would likely have been taken if the merger agreement had
not been executed but which were instead altered, accelerated, postponed or not taken in anticipation of the mergers.

Opinion of Centerview Partners LLC

On September 19, 2016, Centerview rendered to the DTS Board its oral opinion, subsequently confirmed in a written opinion
dated such date, that, as of such date and based upon and subject to various assumptions made, procedures followed, matters
considered, and qualifications and limitations upon the review undertaken by Centerview in preparing its opinion, the merger
consideration to be paid to the holders of Shares (other than Excluded Shares) pursuant to the merger agreement was fair, from a
financial point of view, to such holders.

The full text of Centerview’s written opinion, dated September 19, 2016, which describes the assumptions made, procedures
followed, matters considered, and qualifications and limitations upon the review undertaken by Centerview in preparing its opinion, is
attached as Annex B and is incorporated herein by reference. The summary of the written opinion of Centerview set forth below is
qualified in its entirety to the full text of Centerview’s written opinion attached as Annex B. Centerview’s financial advisory
services and opinion were provided for the information and assistance of the DTS Board (in their capacity as directors and not
in any other capacity) in connection with and for purposes of its consideration of the Transaction and Centerview’s opinion
only addressed the fairness, from a financial point of view, as of the date thereof, to the holders of Shares (other than Excluded
Shares) of the merger consideration to be paid to such holders pursuant to the merger agreement. Centerview’s opinion did not
address any other term or aspect of the merger agreement or the Transaction and does not constitute a recommendation to any
stockholder of DTS or any other person as to how such stockholder or other person should vote with respect to the DTS merger
or otherwise act with respect to the Transaction or any other matter.

The full text of Centerview’s written opinion should be read carefully in its entirety for a description of the assumptions
made, procedures followed, matters considered, and qualifications and limitations upon the review undertaken by Centerview
in preparing its opinion.

In connection with rendering the opinion described above and performing its related financial analyses, Centerview reviewed,
among other things:
 

 
•  a draft of the merger agreement dated September 19, 2016, referred to in this summary of Centerview’s opinion as the “Draft

Merger Agreement”;
 

 
•  Annual Reports on Form 10-K of DTS for the years ended December 31, 2015, December 31, 2014, and

December 31, 2013;
 

 •  certain interim reports to stockholders and Quarterly Reports on Form 10-Q of DTS;
 

 •  certain publicly available research analyst reports for DTS;
 

 •  certain other communications from DTS to its stockholders; and
 

 

•  certain internal information relating to the business, operations, earnings, cash flow, assets, liabilities and prospects of DTS,
including certain financial forecasts, analyses and projections relating to DTS prepared by management of DTS and
furnished to Centerview by DTS for purposes of Centerview’s analysis, which are referred to in this summary of
Centerview’s opinion as the “Forecasts,” and which are collectively referred to in this summary of Centerview’s opinion as
the “Internal Data.”

Centerview also participated in discussions with members of the senior management and representatives of DTS regarding their
assessment of the Internal Data. In addition, Centerview reviewed publicly available financial and stock market data, including
valuation multiples, for DTS and compared that data with similar data for certain other companies, the securities of which are publicly
traded, in lines of business that Centerview deemed relevant. Centerview also compared certain of the proposed financial terms of the
Transaction with the financial terms, to the extent publicly available, of certain other transactions that Centerview deemed relevant, and
conducted such other financial studies and analyses and took into account such other information as Centerview deemed appropriate.

Summary of Centerview Financial Analysis

The following is a summary of the material financial analyses prepared and reviewed with the DTS Board in connection with
Centerview’s opinion, dated September 19, 2016. The summary set forth below does not purport to be a complete description of
the financial analyses performed or factors considered by, and underlying the opinion of, Centerview, nor does the order of the
financial analyses described represent the relative importance or weight given to those financial analyses by Centerview.
Centerview may have deemed various assumptions more or less probable than other assumptions, so the reference ranges
resulting from any particular portion of the analyses summarized below should not be taken to be Centerview’s view of the
actual value of DTS. Some of the summaries of the financial analyses set forth below include information presented in tabular
format. In order to fully understand the financial analyses, the tables must be read together with the text of each summary, as
the tables alone do not constitute a complete description of the financial analyses performed by Centerview. Considering the
data in the tables below without considering all financial analyses or factors or the full narrative description of such analyses or
factors, including the methodologies and assumptions underlying such analyses or factors, could create a misleading or
incomplete view of the processes underlying Centerview’s financial analyses and its opinion. In performing its analyses,
Centerview made numerous assumptions with respect to industry performance, general business and economic conditions and other
matters, many of which are beyond the control of DTS or any other parties to the Transaction. None of DTS, Tessera, Holdco, the
Merger Subs, or Centerview or any other person assumes responsibility if future results are materially different from those discussed.
Any estimates contained in these analyses are not necessarily indicative of actual values or predictive of future results or values, which
may be significantly more or less favorable than as set forth below. In addition, analyses relating to the value of DTS do not purport to
be appraisals or reflect the prices at which DTS may actually be sold. Accordingly, the assumptions and estimates used in, and the
results derived from, the financial analyses are inherently subject to substantial uncertainty. Except as otherwise noted, the following
quantitative information, to the extent that it is based on market data, is based on market data as it existed on or before September 16,
2016 (the last trading day prior to the date of execution of the merger agreement) and is not necessarily indicative of current market
conditions.

Selected Public Trading Analysis

Centerview reviewed and compared certain financial information for DTS to corresponding financial information for the
following publicly traded companies that Centerview, based on its experience and professional judgment, deemed relevant to consider
in relation to DTS:
 

 •  Dolby Laboratories, Inc.
 

 •  Technicolor
 

 •  InterDigital, Inc.
 

 •  TiVo Inc.
 

 •  IMAX Corporation
 

 •  Tessera Technologies, Inc.

Although none of the selected companies is directly comparable to DTS, the companies listed above were chosen by Centerview,
among other reasons, because they are publicly traded companies in the entertainment technology and intellectual property licensing
business that have certain operational, business and/or financial characteristics that, for purposes of Centerview’s analysis, may be
considered similar to those of DTS. However, because none of the selected companies is exactly the same as DTS, Centerview believed
that it was
 

48



8/19/2019 DEFM14A

https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1226308/000119312516744017/d215313ddefm14a.htm 58/256

Table of Contents

inappropriate to, and therefore did not, rely solely on the quantitative results of the selected public company analysis. Accordingly,
Centerview also made qualitative judgments, based on its experience and professional judgment, concerning differences between the
business, financial and operating characteristics and prospects of DTS and the selected companies that could affect the public trading
values of each in order to provide a context in which to consider the results of the quantitative analysis.

Centerview calculated and compared financial multiples for the selected companies based on publicly available information it
obtained from SEC filings, FactSet (a data source containing historical and estimated financial data), and Capital IQ (a data source
containing market data, Wall Street research and analytics) and closing stock prices on September 16, 2016, the last trading day prior to
the date of execution of the merger agreement.

With respect to each of the selected companies, Centerview calculated, among other things, (1) each company’s ratio (a ratio
commonly referred to as a “price earnings ratio,” or “P/E”) of its current stock price to its consensus estimated calendar year 2016 and
2017 earnings per share, referred to in this summary of Centerview’s opinion as “EPS,” adjusted, as DTS discloses in public filings, to
exclude stock-based compensation expense and amortization of intangible assets, referred to in this summary of Centerview’s opinion
as “Adjusted Consensus EPS” and (2) enterprise value (calculated as the fully diluted market value of common equity (determined
using the treasury stock method and taking into account outstanding in-the-money options and other equity awards) plus the book value
of debt and the value of noncontrolling interests less cash equivalents) as a multiple of Wall Street research analyst consensus estimated
earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation and amortization, referred to in this summary of Centerview’s opinion as “EBITDA,”
adjusted to exclude stock-based compensation expense, referred to in this summary of Centerview’s opinion as “Adjusted Consensus
EBITDA,” for calendar years 2016 and 2017.

Discounted Cash Flow Analysis

Centerview performed a discounted cash flow analysis of DTS based on the Forecasts. A discounted cash flow analysis is a
traditional valuation methodology used to derive a valuation of an asset by calculating the “present value” of estimated future cash
flows of the asset. “Present value” refers to the current value of future cash flows or amounts and is obtained by discounting those
future cash flows or amounts by a discount rate that takes into account macroeconomic assumptions and estimates of risk, the
opportunity cost of capital, expected returns and other appropriate factors.

Centerview calculated a range of illustrative enterprise values for DTS by (a) discounting to present value, as of June 30, 2016,
using discount rates from 10.25% to 11.25% (reflecting Centerview’s analysis of DTS’s weighted average cost of capital): (i) the
forecasted fully-taxed unlevered free cash flows of DTS (more information regarding DTS forecasts can be found in the section
entitled “The DTS Merger—Certain Financial Forecasts” beginning on page 43) during the period beginning on July 1, 2016 and
ending on December 31, 2020 and (ii) a range of illustrative terminal values of DTS as of December 31, 2020 calculated by Centerview
applying perpetuity growth rates to DTS’s fully-taxed unlevered free cash flows for the terminal year ranging from 1.0% to 3.0%, and
(b) subtracting from the foregoing results the book value of DTS’s net debt as of June 30, 2016. Centerview divided the result of the
foregoing calculations by the number of fully diluted outstanding shares of DTS common stock based on Internal Data to derive an
implied equity value range for DTS
 

51

common stock to be paid to the holders of shares of DTS common stock (other than Excluded Shares) pursuant to the merger
agreement.

Other Factors

Centerview noted for the DTS Board certain additional factors solely for information purposes, including, among other things, the
following:
 

 
•  Historical closing trading prices of DTS common stock during the 52-week period ended September 16, 2016, the last

trading day prior to the date of execution of the merger agreement, which reflected low and high stock closing prices for
DTS common stock during such period of $20.15 to $34.22 per share of DTS common stock.

 

 
•  Stock price targets for DTS common stock in Wall Street research analyst reports publicly available as of September 16,

2016, which indicated the low and high stock price targets for DTS common stock ranging from $29.00 to $41.00 per share
of DTS common stock.

 

 

•  An analysis of premiums paid in selected transactions in which a public U.S.-based target was acquired since January 1,
2011 in an all-cash transaction valued from $500 million to $1.5 billion and for which premium data was available, in the
high tech, media and entertainment and telecommunications industries. The premiums in this analysis were calculated by
comparing the per share acquisition price in each transaction to, among other things, the closing price of the target
company’s common stock for the date one day prior to the date on which the trading price of the target’s common stock was
perceived to be affected by a potential transaction. Centerview applied the 25th and 75th percentile premiums (25.2% and
46.9%, respectively) of the closing price of the target companies’ common stock on the date one day prior to the applicable
unaffected dates of such transactions to DTS’s closing stock price on September 16, 2016 of $34.05, which resulted in an
implied price range of approximately $42.63 to $50.02 per share of DTS common stock.

 

 

•  An analysis of premiums paid in selected transactions in which a public U.S.-based target was acquired since January 1,
2011 in an all-cash transaction valued from $500 million to $1.5 billion and for which premium data was available, in the
high tech, media and entertainment and telecommunications industries. The premiums in this analysis were calculated by
comparing the per share acquisition price in each transaction to, among other things, the closing price of the target
company’s common stock for the date 52 weeks prior to the date on which the trading price of the target’s common stock
was perceived to be affected by a potential transaction. Centerview applied the 25th and 75th percentile premiums (negative
7.7% and 29.1%, respectively) of the closing price of the target companies’ common stock on the date 52 weeks prior to the
applicable unaffected dates of such transactions to DTS’s 52-week high stock price as of September 16, 2016 of $34.22,
which resulted in an implied price range of approximately $31.59 to $44.18 per share of DTS common stock.

 

 

•  Centerview performed an illustrative analysis of the implied present value of the future value of Company common stock, as
of September 16, 2016. Using each of the Forecasts and consensus estimates, Centerview first derived a range of theoretical
per share values for the shares of DTS common stock (i) as of December 31, 2016 and December 31, 2017 in the case of
consensus estimates and (ii) as of each calendar year end from December 31, 2016 through December 31, 2019, in the case
of the Forecasts, by applying an illustrative Adjusted P/E multiple for the next twelve month period following LTM of 14.1x
(representing DTS’s Adjusted P/E multiple as of September 16, 2016) and 11.7x (representing DTS’s average daily Adjusted
P/E multiple for the year ended September 16, 2016) to estimates of DTS’s Adjusted EPS for the full year, as reflected in
each of the Forecasts and the consensus estimates for each such year, to derive a range of implied equity values for DTS.
Using an illustrative discount rate of 12.4%, reflecting DTS’s estimated cost of equity, Centerview discounted to present
value as of September 16, 2016 the range of theoretical future values it derived as of December 31 of each year of 2016
through 2019 (or 2017 in the case of consensus estimates) to yield illustrative present values per share of DTS common
stock ranging from $28.12 to $51.07.

General

The preparation of a financial opinion is a complex analytical process involving various determinations as to the most appropriate
and relevant methods of financial analysis and the application of those methods to the particular circumstances and, therefore, a
financial opinion is not readily susceptible to summary description. In arriving at its opinion, Centerview did not draw, in isolation,
conclusions from or with regard to any factor or analysis that it considered. Rather, Centerview made its determination as to fairness on
the basis of its experience and professional judgment after considering the results of all of the analyses.

Centerview’s financial analyses and opinion were only one of many factors taken into consideration by the DTS Board in its
evaluation of the Transaction. Consequently, the analyses described above should not be viewed as determinative of the views of the
DTS Board or management of DTS with respect to the merger consideration or as to whether the DTS Board would have been willing
to determine that a different consideration was fair. The consideration for the Transaction was determined through arm’s-length
negotiations between DTS and Tessera and was approved by the DTS Board. Centerview provided advice to DTS during these
negotiations. Centerview did not, however, recommend any specific amount of consideration to DTS or the DTS Board or that any
specific amount of consideration constituted the only appropriate consideration for the Transaction.

Centerview is a securities firm engaged directly and through affiliates and related persons in a number of investment banking,
financial advisory and merchant banking activities. In the past two years, Centerview has been engaged to provide financial advisory or
other services to DTS, and Centerview has received compensation for such services, including in connection with its role as financial
advisor to DTS in connection with DTS’s acquisition of iBiquity Digital Corporation in 2015. In the past two years, Centerview has not
been engaged to provide financial advisory or other services to any of Tessera, Holdco or the Merger Subs, and it has not received any
compensation from any of the Tessera, Holdco or the Merger Subs during such period. Centerview may provide investment banking
and other services to or with respect to DTS, Tessera, Holdco or their respective affiliates in the future, for which Centerview may
receive compensation. Certain (i) of Centerview’s and its affiliates’ directors, officers, members and employees, or family members of
such persons, (ii) of Centerview’s affiliates or related investment funds and (iii) investment funds or other persons in which any of the
foregoing may have financial interests or with which they may co-invest, may at any time acquire, hold, sell or trade, in debt, equity
and other securities or financial instruments (including derivatives, bank loans or other obligations) of, or investments in, DTS, Tessera
or any of their respective affiliates, or any other party that may be involved in the Transaction.

The DTS Board selected Centerview as its financial advisor in connection with the Transaction based on Centerview’s reputation
and experience. Centerview is an internationally recognized investment banking firm that has substantial experience in transactions
similar to the Transaction.

In connection with Centerview’s services as the financial advisor to the DTS Board, DTS has agreed to pay Centerview an
aggregate fee currently estimated to be $13.25 million, $1,000,000 of which was payable upon the rendering of Centerview’s opinion
and the remainder of which is payable contingent upon consummation of the Transaction. In addition, DTS has agreed to reimburse
certain of Centerview’s expenses arising, and to indemnify Centerview against certain liabilities that may arise, out of Centerview’s
engagement.

Interests of DTS’s Directors and Executive Officers in the DTS Merger

In considering the recommendation of the DTS Board that you vote to approve the proposal to adopt the merger agreement, you
should be aware that our directors and executive officers have interests in the DTS merger that are different from, or in addition to,
those of our stockholders generally. The DTS Board was aware of and considered these interests, among other matters, in evaluating
and negotiating the merger agreement and the mergers, and in recommending that the merger agreement be adopted by our
stockholders.

The consummation of the mergers is expected to constitute a “change in control” for purposes of each of the DTS compensation
plans and agreements.
